出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	so from a tedx boston speech , richard risnick told us how genome sequencing is cheap and rapidly disrupting healthcare .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biotech , healthcare , you've got it .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	rl: welcome to the genomic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'm going to show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	so on the left is chromosome 1 .

電磁力和弱力透過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用從而形成這一圖案	the electromagnetic and weak force interacts with matter through hypercharge and weak charge and weak charge , so it forms this pattern .

透過給弱子較大的質量使弱力更加弱	by giving the weak mass to the weak , it makes it weaker .

所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維空間中畫出來然後投影到二維空間以便我們能觀察到	the charges of all known particles can be drawn out in four dimensions and projected into two dimensions so that we can see them .
無論粒子如何作用自然會在這四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡	no matter how particles act , nature keeps perfect balance on these four charge directions .
一個粒子如果和它的反粒子相撞會產生能量四個電荷方向的載荷疊加變為零	if a particle collides with its antiparticles , it creates a charge added to zero charges in the four charge directions .
這樣只要保持能量相同和載荷總量為零可以產生任何物質	this keeps energy the same and the total quantity of charge produces any matter .
比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生	for example , this weak particle and its antiparticle can be created in the collision .

大自然總是會保持完美的平衡	nature always keeps a perfect balance .

強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子裡發生上百萬次使原子核保持一體	strong interactions occur millions of times in every atom of our bodies every second , keeping the atomic nucleus one .

若把它們全部分開會在六維載荷空間中形成漂亮的圖案	and if you take all of them , it's a beautiful pattern in sixdimensional charge space .
在六維空間中將這個圖案進行旋轉我們會發現它十分漂亮	we rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and we find it quite beautiful .
這個圖案把我們已知的自然界在微觀世界中的粒子組成完全呈現出來了	this is a pattern that completely represents the particles that we already know in the microscale world .

其中的一些粒子在實驗中很難看到	some of these particles are very hard to see in experiments .

接下去我想講一下關於未知領域的一些新老觀念	i'm going to move on to some new , old ideas about the unknown .
我們把這個圖案用數學方法進一步擴充套件看看能不能俯瞰全貌	we're going to take this pattern and expand it in a mathematical way , and see if we can look at the whole thing .
我們希望找到構成宇宙的所有種類的粒子和力	we want to find all the particles and forces that make up the universe .
然後在獲得更高能量進行實驗之前用這幅圖案預測新的粒子	and then , before you get higher energy , experimentally , you use this pattern to predict new particles .
量子物理學的舊觀念認為這個不對稱的載荷圖案源於一個更完美的圖案跟希格斯粒子使電弱圖案分裂產生電磁力是一個道理	the old idea of quantum physics is that this asymmetric charge pattern comes from a more perfect pattern with the higgs particles that divide the pattern to generate electromagnetic force .
因此我們要匯入含有新的載荷方向的新的力	so we're going to converge new forces with new charge directions .
在匯入新方向的時候我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉	and as we convey this new direction , we have to guess what charges the particles carry in this direction , and then we can rotate it with other particles .
如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	and if we guess , we can construct the standard charges in sixdimensional charge space as a nonsymmetric concentration of the patterns in sevendimen
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	it was chosen by pati and salam in 1973 as an exploration of the great unified theory .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	and as we look at this new synthetic pattern , we see that there's some space for particles that are supposed to be empty .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is how the unified theory works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists have explored larger and more symmetric structures as subsequent collections .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this much larger configuration allows us to predict the particles that actually exist but aren't observed .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model suggests that these two new types of particles should be similar to the weak force , but they should be more effective .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now we can rotate this episode in seven dimensions , and consider the strange phenomenon of matter in sixdimensional charge space: the second and third generations have the same charge as the first generation .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't identify by corresponding to six charges .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in standard charge space , they overlap each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	however , in eightdimensional charge space , we can give each particle the only new charge .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then rotate in eight dimensions and see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second generation of matter and third generations associated with the first generation through a symmetry known as symmetry .
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular charge pattern in eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group of e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	lee crowds are 248d spaces of smooth curves .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	every point of the pattern can be found in this incredibly complex and beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a tiny fraction of the e8 can be used to describe einstein's general relativity in the distortion of gravity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , together with quantum mechanics , was able to describe everything at the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and this pattern in eightdimensional charge space shows quite beautiful beauty , and it includes thousands of possible interactions between these fundamental particles , each acting as a complex shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	as you rotate it , you can see a lot of the intricate patterns containing them .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	through some kind of spin , we can look at this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful structure , and like all the other unification theories , we can see that there's some blank grids that need new particles to be filled in this pattern .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	and there are 20 of these spaces that need new particles to be filled , two of which have been filled with patty and salaam particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	we know from the pattern where these new particles are like the higgs particles , but they have color charge and interact with the strong force .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	and filling in these new particles makes the pattern complete , giving us the full e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern contains a thick mathematical root .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in mathematics , it's recognized as the most beautiful structure among many people .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	some people predict that this structure with incredibly mathematical beauty can describe the interaction of particles at the smallest scales we can imagine .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematical description of nature isn't just coming out .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature has been presented before us in a language written in mathematics .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it's made up of triangles and circles and other geometric shapes that aren't understood in humanpowered range , and we're going to be lost in the dark labyrinth . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i'm convinced that it's true that i've tried to describe the mathematics of quantum physics using only triangle circles and other geometric shapes .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	and while other physicists and i were studying these things , mathematics was like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we do believe that at the heart of mathematics is a beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	mathematics and quantum mechanics together describe our universe as a growing e8 coral and particles interacting in each position to show beautiful patterns .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	with new machine patterns like the large hadron collider , we might be able to see e8 patterns or other patterns reflect the nature of nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	this process of exploration is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit e8 patterns , that's pretty cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc discovers new particles , but don't fit in this pattern , that's very interesting , although theory is bad for e8 .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and in a way , it's bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	how bad is that ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's very bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but it's always adventurous that nature works .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	it's a theory and a lot of other theories about the following .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	and even with a lot of effort , it doesn't necessarily come natural truths .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	that's how theoretical physics works . it's very common .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	now , new physics theory looks like startup companies .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	after enormous investments , it's emotionally hard to get rid of those failed attempts .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in these uncertainties is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've remained as balanced as possible .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i tried to balance my physics with romantic love and surfing directions of my three charges .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so even if my physics doesn't work , i still have a good life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i'm trying to live in a beautiful place .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	i've spent most of the last decade living on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .
現在我父母最大的謎團是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的	now , the greatest mystery of my parents is how i survived without a fulltime job .

加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	gk: no , it's going to be part of this e8shaped symmetry .

這些化石上 , 從附屬肌肉的形狀上 , 對於那些早期人類的模樣像什麼都能給研究者很多啟示從由他們身邊發現的原始工具上可以看出一些關於他們生活方式的端倪	these fossils , from the shape of the polyglotal muscles , give researchers a lot of revelations , from the primitive tools that they've found around them , on the shape of their life .

當然 , 行為沒有在化石裡體現	of course , behavior doesn't embody the fossils .
他辨稱如果我們發現當代人類在行為模式上與和其最相近的物種巨猿相似或者相同那麼或許這些行為在大概七百萬年前在似猿似人的祖先身上存在過	he recognized that if we find ourselves in a modern mode resembling giant apes similar to their most relevant species , then maybe these behaviors existed in the ancestors of australopithecines about seven million years ago .

當然 , 我給他們起名字 。 他們能活60歲或者更長儘管我們覺得他們中的絕大多數在野生環境活不到60歲	of course , i gave them names . they lived 60 or more , although we think the vast majority of them lived under 60 in the wild .
這是wurzel猩猩 。 母猩猩在11或12歲時生第一個孩子	this is wurzel chimpanzee . females gave birth to their first baby when they were 11 or 12 .
之後每五年或每六年她只生一仔這麼長的童年期內小猩猩很有依賴性 , 需要照料晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上	and every five years or six years , she's got this long childhood , and the baby chimps are very dependent on her , taking care of sleeping with her mom , riding on her back .
我們認為這麼長的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 這牽涉到學習 , 就像童年之於我們一樣	we think this longterm childhood is so important for chimpanzees , and it involves learning , like our childhood .
在各種不同形態動物的進化過程中由於大腦變得日益複雜我們發現 , 在一種個體的生命歷程中學習的作用日益重要	in the process of all different forms of animal evolution , because the brain is becoming more and more complex , we've found that learning is increasingly important in an individual's life .
年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	we now know that they can mimic how they behave .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	and we think it's based on the different kinds of behaviors that we've seen in chimpanzees , in africa , how they've been used in tool use , through observations , imitation and practices , from generations to generations , so we can think of these tool use behaviors as primitive cultures .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have language . we talked about it before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a very rich set of postures and motions , many of which are very similar to us , even identical , and embrace the same meaning that chimpanzees will hug when they say hello .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they're kissed , they're shopping , they're shopping , they'
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also terrifying , or they're still rocking .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzee societies , we find a lot of compassion , love and real although examples .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	unfortunately , like us , they have the dark side of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be incredibly brutal , even like a primordial war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in most cases , these extreme aggressive behaviors are directly targeted to individuals in their neighboring communities .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks are to compete for territory .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's even more helpful than the other creatures , i think , that we recognize that humans and other members of the animal kingdom end up blending boundaries .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very blurry boundary , and as we get more observations , it's always blurred .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	i started my research in 1960 , and i've been doing it now .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees have a complex social life in the wildlife , and most importantly , they help us realize that we are with the animals that we share with us , and that we are part of the planet that cannot be separated from the animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find out that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures in the world , are losing places , like so many others .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the air , and you can see the forest covered in gombe highlands .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i was walking all over the region to realize that outside of the park , this forest stretched along the east coast of tanganyika lake shore in a staggering , coincidental footprint of only 30 square miles of gombe national park , where a problem came into my mind .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we get there to try to save these famous chimpanzees , and people who live around the national park are struggling to survive ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people , not just land , that can bear .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees from burundi emerge from congo crossing lakes , the number of people living there increased .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those are the people who are very , very desperately purchasing other places .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and that's where a plan arose , which we call love .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's about improving people's lives in the village around the lake .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	at first it's small , it's 12 villages . it's 24 .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go into the introduction , but it's a program that includes the raised beds of the elephant wood , and it's applied to the mountains that's currently profoundly eroding approaches to the
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	control , prevent the land from erosion .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	and the way overused farms can be recycled in two years , and these farms can be recycled again .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help the villagers get fresh water from the well .
或許建一些校舍	maybe you build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think it's important to work with smallscale groups of women to give them opportunities for microcredit loans .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	and in the world , we collect about 95 percent of all loans in the world .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	it allows women to work once they're educated , provide scholarships for girls , so they can finish high school , and it's clear that women are educated around the world , and the population is going to decline .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we provided information about planning for birth and aids and their viruses .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and after this project was done , something happened to natural protection .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening with natural protection is that farmers who live in 24 villages haven't looked at us as looking at the whole bunch of monkeys , by the way , a lot of tanzanians , and when we started this project , the village was a tanzanian team .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	i spoke to the villagers as a tanzanian team and asked the villagers what interests them .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in natural protection ? not at all .
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health . they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more about the need for natural conservation .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they're starting to understand that when the higher up the mountains , the horrific land is erosioned and mud streams come .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now , we're developing what we call the gmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is an area outside the national park spontaneously that includes all these different lands that have eroded .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and because these villages live a little bit more standards , they actually agree to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on the high ground so that when the trees come back , the chimps will have green hallways , and they'll be able to wear them so that this is what they need to reproduce and interact with the rest of the community outside the national park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so , the love project succeeded .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we replicated this program in other parts of africa , and in other parts of the wildlands of extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , like all the problems that we've been discussing here at ted for the last few days , the main problem is the main problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poor .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	lots of people live on less fertile land , especially when you cut down the trees and you erode the soil , and the wind erodes , and the desperate people are chopping down more and more trees for themselves and their families , and what happens when things start sacrificing and sacrificing .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	there are other questions , not just in africa , but in all developing worlds , and in all the places on earth , what are we doing to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	the famous scientist , e . o . wilson , said that if everybody on the planet lives on average on the u . s . average , we would need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . but we don't have those , we only have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what's going on ? i mean , the question here is , we might call it the most intelligent life on earth , the wisest brain on earth , that can apply these ted conferences to describe these technologies , but we're destroying one of the only homes .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous peoples around the world would sit together before making important decisions , and ask , " how does this determine affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , it's the important decision that i'm not talking about africa , but rather the developed world that involves millions of dollars and the important decisions that millions of people make , it's just , " how does this affect the next shareholder conference ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	and as i started traveling around africa talking about chimpanzees and their fading forests , i became aware of how so much africa's problems were associated with colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	everywhere , there's these terrible problems .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , and that includes pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air that we breathe constantly poisons us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisoning kills our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water may be one of the biggest problems we have to confront this century , and everywhere , water is polluted by agriculture , industries , home chemicals , and the whole world is still jetting , and the products seem to be failing to profit from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	mangroves are being cut down , and tsunamis are becoming more and more .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we've burned fossil fuels regardless , along with other socalled greenhouse gases , causing climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	eventually , all over the world , people have begun to believe what's going on , that something's wrong with our climate .
全球氣候互相牽連	the interconnected global climate .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the worst impact on the poor is the poor .
已經受影響的是非洲	africa has been affected .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , drought is very severe .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	and when the rain finally rises , it often leads to flooding , and more unfortunately , poverty , hunger and disease all the time .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people who live in in incredible areas of land that can't afford to buy food because they're all stripped of it , so there's no way to leave .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so , with desertification , a little bit of desertification , a little bit of delay , and a little bit of delay , and a little bit of delay
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	it's not just in africa it's all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's surprising that when i travel around the world , so many young people , they look out of hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of indigenous peoples .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i wanted to ask , why is that ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some sort of isolation between the brain and the human heart , in this incredibly brilliant brain ted technique that we've seen here , in a nonscientific term of love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , essentially they're either unacceptable or painful , they're saying the same thing more or less , " it feels like we feel like we've damaged our future and we can't do it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we've certainly destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think how we've damaged this beautiful earth since i was so big , and i've felt this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	so we started this project called roots and shoots , which we've just started , and here , tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is a symbolic root to the ground .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	shoots , shining in the sun , shining through brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks are the kind of environmental and social issues that we're giving the planet , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world can get a breakthrough , make the world a better place for all living things .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots is that each and every day , each of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have a choice , each and every one of us , we have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people are not optional . we need to change those things so that the poor have choices .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the roots and shoots group choose three solutions .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it depends on the age of members , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , to choose different programs .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	essentially , our project now goes from adults to college until more and more adults to building their own roots and shoots group .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different programs between them to create a better world acknowledging that all these different problems are contact and influenced by each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs is going to help them with their own human communities .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and if they can do it , they can raise funds to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their programs is going to help the animals , not just the wildlife , but also the domestic animals .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions is going to help us live in a common environment .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message of all these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , and nations , between cultures , between religious beliefs , between us and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't continue to destroy the world this way .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	just here in africa , just one or two roots and shoots groups are implementing only one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , south africa , congo , brazil , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees , they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they're raising chickens in refugee camps to sell eggs a little bit , or they're just giving eggs to their families and gaining power , because they're growing vegetables and growing chickens no longer dependent on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program was implemented psychologically helpful in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	implementing these programs allows them to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and once again , they become useful members of society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented it in prisons .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time for more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they're also working on aids and their virus .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	it's a very important component of the roots and shoots project , and it's partly accompanied by the old kids talking to the kids .

希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hopefully , the question that i've been asked around the world is this: " jane , you've seen so many terrifying things , and you're watching your chimps decline from about a million to 150 , 000 animals .

藝術家戴安娜•科恩分享關於塑膠汙染對大海和我們日常生活嚴重影響的事實和一些想法 , 幫助大家來擺脫塑膠包圍圈 。	artist diana kahn shared the plastic pollution and the severe and serious ideas of our everyday lives that helped people get out of the plastic surroundings .
consumerism , globalissues , green , missionblue , oceans , plastic	consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , marks , playstics .
戴安娜•科恩diannacohen:關於塑膠汙染的嚴峻事實	diane cohen: the serious truth about plastic pollution .
我是個視覺藝術家 , 也是塑膠汙染聯盟的創始人之一 。	i'm a visual artist , one of the founders of the plastic pollution coalition .
過去20年 , 我一直參與塑膠包的工作 , 我藝術創作的原材料是裁製和縫合塑膠 。	for the last 20 years , i've been involved in plastic packets , and the raw materials my artwork has been tailored and sewn plastic .
讓塑膠變為平面和立體型藝術 , 雕塑和藝術裝置 。	it makes plastics flat and stereo art , sculpture and art installation .
在與塑膠打交道的八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始開裂碎成許多小塑膠塊 。	eight years after dealing with plastic , some of my work began to break into smaller plastic blocks .
我想 , " 好極了 。	and i thought , " great .
塑膠就像我們人類一樣短命 。 "	plastic is like us . "
我自學進一步深入瞭解塑膠 , 我的確瞭解到塑膠是個壞材料 。	i've learned to go a little further into plastic , and i do realize that plastics are a bad material .
塑膠碎成許多小塊 , 但它還是塑膠 , 這很糟糕 。	plastic breaks down into lots of small bits , but it's still plastic , which is terrible .
我們發現有很多塑膠漂浮於大海 。	and we found out that there's a lot of plastic floating in the ocean .
然而在過去的幾年 , 我知道太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。	however , in the last few years , i've known pacific garbage gyres and garbage gyres .
我第一反應--我想這也是多數人的第一反應 , 知道這之後-- " 喔 , 我的上帝 !	and my first reaction i think that's the first reaction to most people , who knows , " oh , my god !
我們要去那裡並清理這些塑膠 。 "	we're going to go there and clean up the plastic . "
所以我提議一隻貨船 , 兩隻退役拖網漁船 , 一臺起重機 , 一臺削片機和一臺冷壓機出海 。	so i proposed a cargo ship , two retreats , a crane , an exploiter and a cold pressure machine out of the sea .
我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	my plan is to navigate to the garbage loop , to raise high respect for the pollution , to start recycling the plastic , cutting it into small slices , then turning it into a plastic chunk , which could be used as an architectural material for the owed community .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	i spoke with people who've been to the garbage duct belt , and they've also studied plastic pollution pollution on marine environments , and after conversations , i've come to realize that shanghai cleaning up plastics compared to the production of plastics worldwide , like the needles of haystacks , i've got to go back and think about looking at the bigger picture .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	the real solution is that we need to find solutions at the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic and oneoffact plastic so that they don't go into the oceans every day around the globe .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know i'm angry .
我並不只關心你也可能想象到的在太平洋中部我們現在所知的 , 權威資料是 , 11個垃圾塑膠環流帶 , 遍及世界五大海洋 。	i'm not just concerned about what you might imagine in the middle of the pacific , but authority data is , 11 junk zones in the ocean , five oceans in the world .
我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just concerned about the plastic loop , but also about the supermarket plastic surrounding .
我要去超市 , 所有事物都是塑膠包裝 。	i'm going to the supermarket , and everything is plastic packaging .
所有飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康的有機市場 。	all beverages are plastic packaging , even healthy organic markets .
我也關注在冰箱的塑膠 , 還有塑膠以及濾取塑膠的毒素被我們吃下和吸收到我們身體裡 。	i'm also concerned about plastic in refrigerators and plastic and toxins that filter plastic are eaten and absorbed in our bodies .
我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a bunch of other people looked at this plastic pollution problem , and built the plastic pollution coalition .
我們為解決這問題開始許多活動 , 它們中的一些是非常簡單的 。	we're starting a lot of activity to solve this problem , and some of them are very simple .
其中一個是:在大海 , 我們發現百分80到百分90海洋廢棄物是塑膠 , 然後我們為什麼不稱其為:	one is: in the ocean , we found 80 to 90 percent of marine waste is plastic , and why don't we call it that ?
再迴圈 。 關於可持續和再迴圈的環保想法的書籍都是類似的觀點 。	textbooks about sustainability and loop are similar opinions .
大家扔東西到垃圾桶裡 , 但是從來沒有再想過此事 。	people were throwing things in the trash , but they never thought about it again .
現實是什麼呢 ?	what is reality ?
在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	in the us , plastic recycling is less than seven percent .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	you want to see , especially when plastic becomes a plastic bottle , the vast majority of plastic bottles are degraded or burned or shipped to china
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be recreated into a plastic bottle , or reused , it's degraded to recycle it so that a plastic bottle is made into small plastic botles so that a plastic botle is no longer recycled into a plastic bot
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a huge problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	one of the things that we've been focusing on and contemplating people is that before three r principles , reduce , reuse , recycle , plus the fourth r , it's rejection use .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you refuse to use one sexual use of plastic and disposable plastic .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there's alternative use , some of them are very oldfashioned .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i myself am now collecting these cool , luxurious glass vessels and replacing them with pleasure privilege and special resistance plastics to store food .
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i knew i was doing it for myself and my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	it's easy to choose to use stainless steel bottles and glass bottles , and you're going to go out with stainless steel bottles and fill it with water or filter it with water , rather than buy plastic bottles of water .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	i guess what i'd like to tell you is that i know that this plastic pollution is a very serious problem for plastic floating in the ocean , but it's a problem for us as consumers , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we've taught people to choose alternative products by raising the consciousness of the problem .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you choose to use replaceable products , you refuse to use one sexual use of plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut the source and stop this plastic pollution into our oceans by saving our oceans , by saving our homes , by saving ourselves .

假設 , 當你在ted遇到某人 , ted , 毫無疑問 , 是每年最佳的社交場所 。 難道你會不跟人家握手 , 然後說: " 你能等一會嗎 ? 我要用手機google一下你 。 "	let's say that when you meet someone at ted , ted , no doubt , the optimal social venue of the year , you don't shake your hand and say , " can you wait ? i google you on my phone . "

所以說 , 我們並沒有一個便捷的渠道去獲取這些資訊 , 這些能幫助我們做出應該要幹什麼的最佳決定的資訊 。	so we don't have a convenient channel to get this information , which helps us make the best decisions that we should do .
因此 , 我的實驗室的研發團隊完成了一系列的發明 , 在不改變使用者行為的條件下 , 幫助使用者快速簡單的獲取這些資訊 。	so , the r&amp ; d team in my lab has completed a series of inventions , and without changing the behavior of the user , helps the user quick access to this information .
現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'm going to show you the device . this is the most successful version of our time , and it's still improving .
我現在正佩戴著我們其實是把市面上常見的一些元件組裝在了一起 。 順便提一下 , 目前這個裝置的成本是350美元 。	i'm wearing now that we're actually assembling some of the common components on the market , and by the way , the cost of this device is 350 dollars .
我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i'm wearing a camera , a simple webcam , a portable battery projector and a small mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these components communicate with my phone in my pocket as a communications and computational device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	in this case , my genius student , pranavmistry , designed and built this entire system .
我們可以看到 , 當他靠近任何表面時 , 資訊就會被投影到表面上 , 他就用雙手來進行操作 。	we can see that when he gets closer to any surface , the information gets projected onto the surface , and he operates with his hands .
系統會跟蹤四個主要的手指 。	the system will follow four of the primary fingers .

進行慣常體力運動 , 是他們享受這些事情的時候 。 他們常常步行 , 這被證明是防止認知降低的唯一方法 , 並且他們人人有花園 。	regular physical exercise is when they enjoy these things , and they walk a lot , and it's proven to be the only way to prevent cognitive decline , and they have gardens .
他們知道如何安排生活因此有正確的觀點 。	they know how to arrange life so that they have the right perspective .
每種文化都不慌不忙地變換 。	cultures are busy changing .
撒丁島人祈禱 。 再生論者也祈禱 。	sardinians pray . regeneratives pray .
沖繩人有祖先祭拜的規約 。	the flusher has the ancestors' rules .
但是你的匆忙或壓力引發的炎症反應這些都與老年痴呆症和心血管疾病都有關係的 。	but your hurried or stressinduced inflammatory responses all have to do with aging dementia and cardiovascular disease .
每天減緩行動15分鐘這種炎症就能變成一種反炎症狀態 。	by slowing down 15 minutes a day , this inflammation becomes a state of antiinflammation .
沖繩人把這個目的感叫做有意義的生活 。	the hedgeists call this purpose a meaningful life .
一個人一生中最危險的兩年一是出生的時候 , 因為嬰兒死亡率高另外就是退休的時候	the two most dangerous years of a person's life were born because of infant mortality , and then retirement .
這些人知道他們的生活目的感他們生活活躍 , 能有7年的額外壽命 。	these people know their sense of purpose in their lives , and they live a life of seven extra years .
沒有長壽食品	there's no longevity food .
這些人每天就喝一點酒 , 酒是不用強行賣給美國人的 。	these people drink a little bit of wine a day and don't sell it to americans .
哈哈他們常吃蔬菜食品	haha , they eat vegetables a lot .
不是說不吃肉但是吃很多豆類和堅果 。	not eating meat but eating lots of beans and nuts .
他們有辦法避免飲食過量 , 幾乎沒有什麼能把他們推向餐桌 。	they were able to avoid overeating , almost nothing pushes them to the dinner table .
這些的根本是他們如何聯絡 。	it's essentially how they contact .
把家庭放在第一位 , 照顧孩子和年邁的父母 。	they put their families in the first place , and they took care of their children and their elderly parents .
他們的社群建立在誠信基礎上 , 這個能增加4到14年的生命 。 當然 , 你一月至少要做四次才可以 。	their community is built on the basis of integrity , which will increase life for four to 14 years , and of course you need to do it at least four times in january .
這裡最重要的事情是他們屬於一個正義的群體 。	the most important thing here is that they belong to a justice group .
他們或者生在正義之家或者是主動和正義之士呆在一起 。	they might be born in a justice house or in an active and justice house .
從弗雷明翰研究中我們得知如果你有三個好朋友都肥胖你也有一半肥胖的可能 。	we know from the fremenham studies that if you have three good friends , you're half obese .
所以如果你和不健康的人在一起隨時間推移會受到很大影響 。	so if you're with unhealthy people , it's going to be a huge impact over time .
如果你朋友娛樂的主意是體力活動 , 打保齡球或打曲棍球腳踏車或園藝工作 , 他們飲酒適量飲食適度 , 他們投入工作值得信任 , 最後就會對你產生最大影響 。	if your friend's entertainment ideas are physical activities , bowling or playing hockey bicycles or gardening , they drink alcohol appropriately , they're trustworthy , and they end up having the biggest impact on you .
食物沒有什麼用 , 歷史上沒有一種食物能養活2%的人口 。	there's nothing to use for food , there's no food in history that feeds two percent of the population .
練習專案通常在一月開始十月結束 。	practice projects usually end in january .
至於長壽 , 沒有藥片或其他什麼東西能在短期內奏效 。	and in terms of longevity , no pills or anything else can be done in the short term .
但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends as the longterm adventures , it's the most important thing that you do to increase your lifespan and keep life alive .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	and the ink that conducts electricity , the yaw , the transparency windows , the jelly that plays music these things actually exist . catarina mota says now it's time to try them . mota will take us through this new and magical material , and she says , the best way to make sense of these materials is to try and experiment with them and try and enjoy them .
creativity , design , technology	it's ivity , it's serious . it's serious .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: play with smart materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather used a bicycle and a washing machine to convert it into a car for rides for his family .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly because he knew how to modify it .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	at one point , we've all understood some mechanical principles of how they're made , so we can make them ourselves and maintain them , or at least based on our understanding of wise purchasing decisions .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these diy's practical skills were lost in the second half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but right now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing the principles and the knowledge of the objects back to our lives , and i believe we need to bring that knowledge to the next level , the components of understanding these objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of , and how they're produced .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some remarkable future complex materials such as modular plastics , conductive paint , changeable pigments and glowing fabrics .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to discard the traditional printed circuit boards or wires directly draw circuit boards using conductive inks .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	this little device that i'm holding in my hands is we're using conductive inks to make a touch sensor , and once exposed to the human skin , this little light will light up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	conductive inks have been used by artists , and the latest progress has been shown soon that we can apply them to laser printers and laser lasers .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a paper that's bathed in bright colorless pellets of light .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed a regular acet is a phenomenon just around its edge , and this one immersed a photoreal acrylic , which illuminates the entire piece of paper when we turn on the lights .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been used indoor design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermochromic pigment changes color in certain temperatures .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this thing in a temperature temperature temperature a little higher than the outside world , and you can see what happens .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	in addition to other purposes , this material is mostly made of baby bottles , and it tells you when things get cold and drinkable .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we usually call smart materials .
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they're going to be applied to lots of objects and technological products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not have science fiction yet to guarantee flying cars , but we can have walls that are temperatured , keyboards that can be rolled up , and with a shutter that's very transparent .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	now , i'm a social scientist from coban , and why am i talking about smart materials today ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they make things , and i'm convinced that we should know a lot more about the materials that make up our world , and that we know very little about these hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's very little information about how to use these materials , and they're much less information about how to make them .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	currently , most of them are in trade secrets and patents , only universities and large companies can acquire .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so over three years ago , i started a project called open maternals with kirsty boy .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we're sharing experiments with anyone who wants to join us , releasing information , encouraging others to contribute and collect resources like research papers and like our producers .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we'd like to take this website and make it a largescale , collective database and gather information with smart materials , diy .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how smart materials work and what they're made out of ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we can't influence things that we don't understand , things that we don't understand and don't use reversely affect us .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things that we use , the clothes that we we wear , the house that we live in , have a profound impact on our behavior , our health and our quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made up of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation always comes from craftsmanship .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	oftentimes , amateur lovers , not experts , have invented and improved things like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge in material science is its complexity and its demand for expensive instruments .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper on making conductive inks in a simpler way .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordan bonker , before this experiment , was a person who had no chemistry experience , and he read this paper and repeated it using the existing substances and tools in his workshop .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he used a oven , and he even organized a vortex mixer on the basis of another scientist/manufacturer .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	later , jordan published his experiments online , including all the unsuccessful things he tried so that others could learn and replicate the experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment done in a university garage in chicago using cheap materials and tools to repeat that experiment .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	based on the results he published , others can then do and design even simpler steps and improvements .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i'd like to share with you of her project is that she focuses on the creativity and manufacturing skills of producers as well .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	the electric tools are very powerful in teaching us how things work , but the constraints that they inherit in their designs are influencing the way that we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so the hannah approach , on the other hand , is to create a series of technologies to create very normative things by teaching us the materials themselves to liberate us from predetermined constraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorites in hannah's many admirable experiments .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " speech paper " ] what we're seeing here is just a copper line on a piece of paper with an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	at mit , professor marcelocoelho studied all kinds of materials , hannah used all kinds of materials to create a series of paper speakers , from regular copper to conductive fabrics and inks .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan , like so many other makers , hannah published her recipe and allowed anyone to come and repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but electrons on paper are one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap and flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hand job shared her discovery with her , opening a door to a new array of possibilities that are both aesthetic and innovative .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	the interesting thing about makers is that we're creating passion and curiosity , and we're not afraid of failure .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we typically deal with problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we end up finding alternatives or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to do experiments with new materials , more researchers are willing to share their work ; more manufacturers will share their knowledge , and we'll have a better chance to create technology that will benefit us all .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like tednelson in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at the time , computers were these big machines that scientists were concerned about , and nobody would dream of putting in a home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i stand here today and i say , " you need to understand smart materials a little bit strange . "
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	keep in mind that the pioneering knowledge of emerging technologies is to ensure that we have the best way to rhetoric in the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	when we drive the car , we sit in a glass bubble , and we lock the door , and we step on the gas and we navigate ourselves , even though we only see a few cars in the back of the car , but if the car exchanges data about position , speed , and we use models to model the safest route for every driver , and jennifer hay's mind a zero accident .
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer hay: car accidents or inevitably .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face it: driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , those gods , peace and security around the world , have put them on top of the dashboard , which inadvertently reveals a fact that we all care about .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the cause of death , especially in the united states between the ages of 16 and 19 , and 75 percent of all car accidents have nothing to do with drug accidents and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one could give the exact answer , but i remember the first time i got in a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new driver when i was driving outside on the highway , and i suddenly saw the brake lights in front of me .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	bachi brendton was planning to live and travel across the country for a year , but when depressed and free writers worked soup , his travel camp became homeless , and in this beautiful speech , she described a unique experience of being a homeless worker in the us .

貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	bjk: one year i'm homeless .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , i'm a journalist , i'm also a very intense person , so i learned a lot of novelty over 22 years as a journalist .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and one of the things i learned about three years ago was that i became invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died that february , and i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	he died very , very attacked me .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and this was because there were a lot of things that i wanted to perceive and deal with .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i was camping every day for travel , and decided to live for a year in a suv for a longterm camp .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rotwell dog and camping equipment , downloaded it to chevy in 1975 , driving to the sunset , but i had no idea of three serious things at the time .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: societies will be equal to the value of human beings at a very small scale .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i'm not aware of how severe the negative effects of other people's words are on us if we let go .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i'm not aware of homelessness as a lifestyle , not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	it's nice to live in a car at first .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was bathing the showers , and i was walking out to eat .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and it's time to express emotions .

我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my freedom of writers ended , and i needed to get a fulltime job to pay my bill .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	from a very gentle spring to a very hot summer , what happens to a very hot summer .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	regardless of where the car park is unbearable , i'm obviously carrying a cat and a dog , and it's very hot .

在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	at night , temperatures are rarely cooled to below 80 degrees fahrenheit , which makes me almost impossible to sleep .

我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i didn't know when or how it happened , and i quickly went from being a talented writer to being a homeless woman living in a car that was incredibly fast .

當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when some homeless people realized that , including a professor who used to teach in college , they said , " you're not homeless , what's the reason you're here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people didn't see me as homeless people , but i did .

真正無家可歸的人並沒有希望可言 。 "	there's no hope for a real homeless person . "
診所針對我沮喪開的藥物的副作用讓我有點自殺的傾向 。 我還記得當時想 , " 如果我自殺了 , 可能沒人會發現的 "	the doctor's side effects of the despairing medication made me a little bit suicidal , and i remember thinking , " if i kill myself , no one's going to discover it . "
在那不久後 , 我的一個朋友就告訴我 , 她聽說提姆路塞特 , 一個全國知名的記者在全國播放的電視節目上談論到了我 。	not long after that , a friend of mine told me she heard about tim luther , a nationally renowned journalist talking about me on national television .
一篇我寫的關於我父親的短文 , 在他去世前一年寫的 , 被收錄到了提姆的新書裡 。	an essay i wrote about my father , written about a year before he died , was in tim's new book .
他那時在做巡迴演講 , 提到我的寫作 。	he was giving a speech tour and referring to my writing .
當我發現提姆路塞特 , 前meetthepress節目的調解員 , 在談論我的寫作 。 而我卻生活在停在沃爾瑪停車場裡的旅行車裡面 , 我開始笑了 ,	when i found tim luther , former meetthe press , talking about my writing , and i was living inside the walmart parking lot , i started laughing .
我開始笑 , 因為這正是問題根結 , 我是一位作家呢 , 還是一位無家可歸的女人 ?	i started laughing , because that's the question at the end: am i an author , or is it a homeless woman ?
於是我走進一家書店 。 找到提姆的書 。	so i went into a bookstore . i found tim's book .
我站在那 , 又重新讀了一遍我寫的短文 。	and i stood there and i readvised the essay i wrote again .
因為我是一位作家 ,	because i'm a writer .
是一位作家 。	it's a writer .
在那之後 , 我很快就搬回了田納西 。	since then , i quickly moved back to tennessee .
有時住在車裡 , 有時會去朋友家睡沙發 。	sometimes in the vehicle , sometimes they go to a friend's house to sleep with a couch .
我又重新開始寫作了 。	i started writing again .
在接踵而來的夏天裡 , 我又成為了一名新聞記者 。	and in the summer after that , i became a journalist again .
我得了獎 , 住在我自己的公寓裡 。	i got a winner and lived in my own apartment .
我不再無家可歸 。	i was no longer homeless .
我也不再被無視 。	i was no longer blinded .
無數的人在從事著全職和兼職的工作 , 而且住在他們的車裡 。	countless people are engaged in fulltime and parttime jobs and living in their cars .
但是社會還繼續汙衊他們並視住在交通工具裡或者睡在街上為犯罪 。	but society continued to sit where they lived and lived in transportation or slept in the streets for crime .
所以那些無家可歸 , 有工作但是無家可歸的人 , 大部分還是隱藏著的 。	so the homeless , the workforce , the homeless , the vast majority are still hidden .
但是如果你見到了 , 僱用他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給予他們希望 。	but if you see them , hire them , encourage them and give them hope .
只要有希望 , 人類的精神可以克服一切困難 。	with hope , the human spirit can overcome everything .
我並不是來這裡為無家可歸的人做宣傳的 。	i'm not here to campaign for the homeless .
我不是來這裡鼓勵你們去施捨下一個你見到的乞丐 。	i'm not here to encourage you to give away the next beggar that you see .
而我在這裡是來告訴你們 , 根據我過去的經歷 , 人不是由他們所住的地方 , 睡得地方 , 或者他們在任何一個時間的生活狀態所決定的 。	and i'm here to tell you that , based on my past experience , people are not determined by the places where they live or the places where they sleep or where they live in any given moment .
三年前 , 我住在一個停在沃爾瑪的停車場的汽車裡 。 而今天我卻在ted演講 。	three years ago , i lived in a car that parked in walmart , and today i'm speaking at ted .
希望永遠 , 永遠 , 會指引前路 。 謝謝 。	hopefully forever , always , always will guide the way . thank you .
在tedxchange系列中 , 泰國的 " 安全套之父 " , mechaiviravaidya向觀眾展示泰國在二十世紀七十年代如何採取大膽的措施來提高人民的生活水平 。 控制人口是他們的首要任務 。 他的演講圍繞安全套展開 , 直爽風趣 , 也發人深省 。	in the tedxchange series , " the father of the thailand security condom , " mechai viravidya showed thailand how to adopt a bold purpose in the '70s to raise the average living standards of the people in the '70s .
culture , globalissues , health , population , science	those are the global isisues , the ones that are there , the ones that are there .
mechaiviravaidya:套套先生 , 讓泰國更美好	mechai viravaidya: mr . suits , make thailand better .
四十年前 , 我還是個年輕小夥子的時候 , 這個國家非常 , 非常窮 。 無數人過著貧困的生活 。	when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor , and so many people lived in poverty .
我們決心改變這一切 , 但我們沒有實施任何福利政策 , 或者扶貧計劃 。	we're changing it , but we're not implementing any welfare policy or antipoverty programs .
我們開始推行計劃生育政策 , 採取了一套非常成功的母子保健措施 , 多項措施 。	we started launching fertility policy initiatives , taking a very successful set of mothers' children's healthcare measures , multiple measures .
總的來說 , 如果孩子出生後不能存活 , 自然不會有人接受計劃生育 。	in short , if the child is born unable to survive , it's not natural to be planned to fertilize .
所以 , 第一步就要保證孩子和母親的生活 , 然後實行計劃生育 。	so the first step is to guarantee the children and mothers' lives and then plan them for reproduction .
光控制嬰兒的死亡率是不夠的 , 你還需要計劃生育 。	it's not enough to control babies' mortality , and you need to plan for birth .
我帶大家回顧一下當初我們為什麼要採取這個政策 。	let me take you back to why we took this policy in the first place .
1974年 , 在我的國家裡	in 1974 , in my country .

根本沒有未來可言 。	there is no future at all .

這非常好 , 但是這也只能幫助全國20%的地區 。	it's very good , but it's also about 20 percent of the country .

不 , 我們決定做出更多努力 。	no , we decided to do more work .

1975年 , 我們開始推行首個小額貸款政策 。 做籌劃工作的婦女們說: " 我們只貸款給那些進行節育的婦女 。	in 1975 , we launched the first microcredit policy , and the women who raised the planning said , " we only gave birth control to women .

我敢保證如果婦女們一起工作相互聯絡 , 智慧並且受到過教育能夠為這個星球帶來和平和繁榮	i'm sure if women work together , they're intelligent , they're educated to bring peace and prosperity to the planet .
在當今的任何戰爭中 , 大多數受害者是平民主要是婦女和小孩 。 他們是被動受害者	in any war today , most victims are democratic if women and children are passive .
男性主宰世界 , 然後看著我們所帶來這一切	men dominate the world and look at what we're bringing .
到底我們需要怎麼樣的世界	what kind of world do we have to live in ?
這是一個我們常常捫心自問的問題	it's a question that we ask ourselves all the time .
這對已有世界秩序行得通嗎 ?	does it work for the world order already ?
我們需要一個珍重生命的世界並且每人都能夠有豐富多彩的生活而不僅僅是特權者的權力	we need a world where privileging life matters , and each one can afford to live a rich and colorful life , not just the privileged .
一月份我參觀了費爾南多.波特羅的繪畫展覽在柏克利大學的圖書館中	in january , i visited a painting exhibition from fernando portro in the library of berkeley .
在美國除了紐約展覽廳沒有博物館或展覽廳會展示波特羅的作品他們沒有膽量展示這些繪畫因為繪畫主題是關於阿布格萊布監獄	in the united states , there's no museum , no exhibition , except new york hall , showing portero's work , and they don't have the dare to show these paintings , because the painting title is about
展覽有著大量的虐待和侮辱的繪畫在浩繁的波特羅風格中	the exhibition had lots of paintings of abuse and insult in the vast porto style .
我沒有辦法得到這些圖象從我的腦海中或者心中	i couldn't get these images from my mind or from my mind .
我最害怕的是不純潔的力量	what i'm most afraid of is the power of impurity .
我害怕力量的濫用以及力量所造成的暴力	i was afraid of the abuse of power and the abuse of violence .
在我們的種族中 , 男人們定義現實然後逼迫他人接受現實遵守規則	in our ethnicity , men define reality and force others to accept reality and follow the rules .
規則常常發生變化 , 但總是對男性有益就這樣 , 在一致遵循的狀況下在經濟上並不成立的規則卻完美地存在	rules are constantly changing , but they're always beneficial to men , and that's how unanimously economically imperfect rules are perfectly occurring .
從上到下 , 一層層的力量濫用	from top to bottom , a layer of force abuses .
女性和兒童 , 尤其是貧窮的 , 就這樣處於底層	women and children , especially poor , are at the bottom .
即使是最一無所有的男人也有人被他凌虐常常是婦女或者兒童	even the most outofthebody men have been abused by them , often women and children .
我再也受不了少數人操縱多數人透過性別 , 收入 , 種族和階級的手段	i was very suffering from a few manipulated , most people through gender , income , race and class .
我認為現在時機已經成熟可以根本性地改變我們的文明	i think it's time to mature , to fundamentally change our civilization .
不過若要真正改變 , 就需要讓婦女的力量參與到世界當中	but to really change it takes women's strength to get involved in the world .
我們需要讓足夠的婦女擁有權力並且培養男人心中的婦女力量	we need to get enough women to have power and cultivate women's strength in men .
這裡當然是指年輕男人了	and this is , of course , young men .
老男人們都沒求了 , 只能等著他們死光	the old guys didn't get it , they just waited for it .
的確我也想擁有索菲亞羅蘭的長腿和著名的酥胸	and indeed , i wanted to have the long legs of sophia loren and the famous chest .
不過若是可以選擇 , 我寧願擁有勇敢的心像旺加里.馬塔伊 , 蘇曼麗.馬恩 , 珍妮和羅斯.馬培德那樣的	but if i had a choice , i would rather have the courageous hearts like wangari mathai , somali marian , jenny and rose mabedd .
我想讓世界變得更好	i wanted to make the world a better place .
不僅僅是消極地等待改變 , 而是參與改變	it's not just negative ; it's changing . it's changing .
為什麼不這樣 ? 這是能夠做得到的 。 看看這裡 , 充滿了知識 , 活力 , 才華和科技	why not ? it's possible . look here , it's full of knowledge , it's dynamic , it's technologies .
讓我們走出冷氣房 , 捲起袖子開始行動 , 帶著我們的熱情創造一個近乎完美的世界	let's get out of the cold gas , roll up our sleeves , start acting , carrying our enthusiasm to create an almost perfect world .
在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city that's that big in london , it costs up to 30 million tons of food every day , but where does it come from , architect carolyn steel , to talk about the myths of feeding a city every day , about how food transportation affects the formation of cities and development of the city .
cities , culture , food , globalissues	you know , fixes , you know , the world issues .
carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市	carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities .
如何餵養一個城市 ?	how do you feed a city ?
這是我們這個時代的一個重大問題之一 。	this is one of the great questions of our time .
然而很少人會問這個問題 。	however , very few people ask that question .
我們習以為常了 , 我們走進商店的時候走進餐廳的時候 , 或是一個小時後我們進入這個劇院的門廳總會有食物等著我們它們很神奇地從某個地方冒出來	we used to think that when we walked into the shop , when we walked into the restaurant , when an hour later , we entered the theater gates , there was always food , and they waited for us , amazingly emerging from somewhere .
然而 , 當你想像每一天 , 在一個倫敦那麼大的城市 , 要生產足夠的食物運輸、交易這些食物 , 烹飪 , 食用 , 最後扔棄它們而且類似的事情每天都發生著在地球上的每一個城市都如此每個城市都有食物供應 , 這件事很不可思議	and yet , when you imagine that every single day in a city the size of london , enough food transportation , all these foods , cooking , finally throwing them out , and things like that happen every day every day , every city on the planet , every day , so much food supply , this is incredible .
我們住在每天有食物供應的城市 , 彷彿這是世界上最自然的事情 , 我們忘記了我們也是動物 , 所以我們需要進食 , 事實上我們要依賴自然界就如同我們的祖先要依賴自然界一樣 。	we live in a city where we have food supply every day , as if it was the most natural thing in the world , and we forgot that we are animals , so that we need to eat , and that we actually depend on nature as our ancestors rely on nature .
隨著我們越來越多人到城市生活 , 越來越多的自然界正在變成我身後的這些特別的景象這是巴西matagrosso的大豆田用來種食物養活我們	as more and more of us go to cities , more and more natural worlds are becoming these extraordinary landscapes that i'm seeing here in brazil , matagroso , to grow our food .
這些特別的景象我們很少人親眼目睹過	these particular scenes are very , very few of us have ever seen .
越來越多的這些地貌不只是生產食物養活我們	more and more of these landscapes aren't just producing food to feed us .
隨著我們越來越多人移居城市越來越多人吃肉所以每年全球有三分之一的糧食現在是用來餵動物而不是餵養我們人類	as more and more of us move into cities , more and more people eat meat , so that a third of the world's food is now fed to animals rather than feeding us humans .
雖然說需要3倍的糧食事實上卻是10倍的食物來餵養一個人 , 如果從餵養動物的糧食也計算在內這並不是一個很有效率的餵養方式	and even though it takes three times more food , it's actually 10 times more food to feed one person , and if you feed the animals , it's not a very efficient way of feeding the animals .
這是一個越來越重要的問題	it's an increasingly important question .
到2050年 , 預測有兩倍的人口將在城市居住	by 2050 , it's predicted that twice as many people are going to live in cities .
預測到也將需要兩倍的肉和奶類製品的消耗	it's predicted that we're going to need twice as much meat and milk products .
所以肉的消耗和城市化是共同發展的	so meat consumption and urbanization are coevolving .
這就將引發一個很重大的問題	and that leads to a huge problem .
要餵養60億的飢餓人口在2050年	to feed six billion hunger people in 2050 .
這是個大問題.如果我們還像我們現在這麼發展 , 我們很可能沒法在2050年解決這個問題	it's a big problem . if we're still as evolving as we are , we're probably not going to be able to solve this problem by 2050 .
每年有1900萬公頃的雨林消失它們用作開墾新的耕地	every year , 19 million hectares of rainforest disappear , and they use it to reclaim new arable land .
儘管與此同時我們也失去等量的現有耕地 , 因為鹽鹼化或水土流失	although at the same time , we're losing equal arable land because of saltification or water plummeting .
我們也急需化石燃料	we desperately need fossil fuels .
在歐洲 , 我們需要10卡路里的能量來生產1卡路里為我們消耗的食物	in europe , we need 10 calories of energy to produce one calories of food for us .
儘管這些食物我們都是花了很多功夫才生產出來事實上我們卻不珍惜它們	despite all of these foods , it took a lot of effort to produce them , and in fact we don't value them .
在美國有一半食物被扔棄	half of the food was discarded in the united states .
最終 , 在這漫長過程的最後我們將沒法養活我們這個地球	ultimately , at the end of this long journey , we're not going to be feeding our planet .
我們中10億人肥胖 , 還有多於10億的人處於飢餓中	one billion of us are obese , and more than one billion are hungry .
這些都沒有道理	none of this makes any sense .
當你發現現在80%的全球食物貿易僅由五家跨國公司控制 , 這是挺可怕的	when you find out that 80 percent of global food trade is controlled by five multinational companies , it's terrifying .
隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界正在接受西方的飲食	as we move to cities , the world is accepting western diet .
如果我們展望未來這不是個可持續的飲食方式	if we look at the future , it's not a sustainable way of eating .
我們怎麼會走到這一步 ?	how did we get here ?
更重要的是 , 我們應該怎麼做 ?	and more importantly , what do we do ?
先回答那個較簡單的問題 , 首先我想說 , 在大概1萬年前是這個過程的開始在古代的中東地區也就是廣大的新月狀的地區	well , to begin with , the simpler question , i would say , is that it was started about 10 , 000 years ago in the middle east , which is the vast region of the new month .
因為你可以看到它是新月形的	because you can see it's the new moon .
同時它也是廣大的	and it's also vast .
就在這裡 , 大概1萬年前2大偉大的發明農業和城市化在此發生幾乎在同時 , 同一地點	here it is , about 10 , 000 years ago , when 20 great inventions were happening , agriculture and urbanization , almost at the same time , at the same time .
這並不是偶然因為農業和城市是緊密聯絡的.它們需要彼此	it's not accidentally because agriculture and cities are very closely communicated , and they need each other .
因為糧食的發現我們的遠古祖先 , 第一次第一次生產出足夠的糧食並且產量穩地 , 這幫助他們長期居住下來	and because of food discovery , our distant ancestors first produced enough food for the first time , and yielded steady , which helped them live longtermly .
如果我們看一下當時那些居住地我們可以看到他們是緊密的	if we look at the places where they were living at the time , we can see that they were very close .
他們被農田圍繞並由一些大的廟宇統領著例如這一個在烏爾的神殿事實上 , 他們是很有效的精神統領 , 食物分發中心 , 兩者結合	they're surrounded by farms , and they're led by large temples , such as this temple in ur , and in fact , they're very effective , very spiritual , food distribution centers , combined .
因為這些神殿組織耕作收集這些糧食 , 供奉給諸神然後把諸神沒吃的食物發還給人們	because the temple tissue cultures are collecting these foods , giving them to the gods , and then giving them back the food that the gods haven't eaten .
所以這些城市的精神和物質生活都用糧食和收成掌控並維持城市的生活	so the spirit and the material life of these cities is used to eat and control and maintain the city's lives .
事實上 , 過去的每個城市都是如此	in fact , every city in the past has been like this .
當然 , 並不是每個都是那麼小的城市	now , of course , not every city is that small .
比如很著名的羅馬城有大約100萬居民在公元一世紀的之前	rome , the famous city of rome , has about a million residents before the 1500s .
那麼 , 這樣的城市是如何維持供給的呢 ?	so how do such a city sustain itself ?
在我眼裡 , 我把答案稱作 " 古老的城市之路 "	in my eyes , i call it " the path of ancient city . "
基本上 , 羅馬有通往海洋的道路這樣使從很遠的地方進口食物成為可能	rome basically has a road to the ocean , and it makes it possible to import food from a very far away .
這樣是在古代能實現的唯一的方法因為陸上運輸相當困難鑑於路況不好	it's the only way that we've been able to do this in the ancient world , because shipping is quite difficult because it's bad for the road .
而且食物的消耗是很快的	and the consumption of food is fast .
所以羅馬常常發動戰爭攻打像迦太基和埃及那樣的國家僅僅是為了得到他們的糧食儲備	so romans often launched war attacks in countries like ghachi and egypt just to get their food reserves .
其實 , 事實上 , 你可以把帝國的擴張理解為一種長期的軍事化的購物狂歡	in fact , you can understand the empire's expansion as a sort of longterm militarized shopping madness .
事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 。 我不得不指出的是羅馬在一個時期 。 我認為這非常特別	in fact , i love that fact . i have to argue that rome was in a period . i think that's very special .
所以羅馬形成自己的海岸線根據他的口味	so rome formed his own coastline , based on his flavor .
但是還有一件有趣的事情發生在前工業化的世界	but there's another interesting thing that's happening in preindustrialized worlds .
如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖我們可以看見作物從泰晤士河畔出產的位於地圖的底部	if we look at maps of london in the 17th century , we can see crops coming out of the thames' river banks and on the bottom of the map .
因為市場在城市的南部	because the market is in the south of the city .
道路從那裡通向主要消費市場戚普塞街這裡也是糧食的主要消費市場	roads are all the way from there to mainstream consumer , relatives purse street , which is the main consumer market for food .
如果我們隨便看看這裡的一條街道的名字bread街 , 你可以明白三百年前這裡都發生了什麼	if we just look at a street here , bread street , you can see what was happening here 300 years ago .
這個道理同樣使用於魚類	it's also used in fish .
魚當然是從河裡面打撈出來的	the fish , of course , came out of the river .
billlingsgate是倫敦有名的賣魚市場在1980年之前	billlingsgate was a famous selling fish market in london before 1980 .
這是很特別的 , 真的 , 當你仔細想想	it's quite extraordinary , really , when you think about it .
每個人都在這裡遊蕩拿著像轉頭一樣的大哥大還有 , 在港口還有發臭的魚	everybody's wandering around with big brotherhoods and stinky fish in the port .
這是在城市中關於食物的另一件事情一旦一種食物在某個城市站穩腳跟它的地位很難被動搖	and this is another thing about food in the city: once a food is stabilized in a certain city , it's very difficult to shake it .
肉是一個非常不同的故事了因為 , 動物自己走向城市	meat is a very different story because animals go to cities themselves .
因此 , 倫敦消費的大量肉類是從西北方過來的從蘇格蘭和威爾士	so london consumed a lot of meat consumption from the northwest , from scotland and wales .
當他們過來 , 抵達城市的西北方這就說明了為什麼smithfield倫敦一個非常有名的肉類市場 , 在這裡產生	when they came and arrived in the northwest , this explained why smithfield london was a very famous meat market in the city that was produced here .
家禽從anglia的東部來 , 去往東北部	domestic avian comes from angolia to the northeast .
我感覺這有點像一個天氣播報員然後鳥兒都飛過來了它們的腳被小帆布鞋包裹著	i felt a bit like a weather announcer , and the birds flew over , and their feet were wrapped in tiny canvases .
然後當它們在東部降落的時候具體說來是在戚普塞街 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方這也就是戚普塞街被稱為 " 家禽 " 街的原因	and when they landed in the eastern landing , they specifically described what they were selling , which is why they called " domestic " street .
事實上 , 如果你看看任何一個城市的地圖在工業化時代之前你能夠發現食物是如何進入城市的	in fact , if you look at any map of any city before the industrial era , you can see how food enters the city .
事實上 , 你可以看出食物是如何塑造一個城市的透過閱讀街道的名稱 , 你就會發現很多線索	in fact , you can see how food shapes a city by reading the name of the street , and you'll see a lot of clues .
星期五街 , 在過去的日子中是一個在星期五買魚的地方	friday street , in the past , was a place to buy fish on friday .
但是 , 你同時也必須想象那裡到處都是食物	but at the same time , you have to imagine that there's food everywhere .
因為街道和公共區域是食物買賣的唯一地點	because the streets and the public areas are the only places for food purchasing .
如果你想象一下1830年的smithfield你會發現很難在這樣一個城市裡面生活下去並且不留意食物的來源	if you think about smithfield in 1830 , it's very difficult to live in a city like this without paying attention to the source of food .
事實上 , 當你在星期日吃午飯的時候你將很有可能聽到窗外的牛羊的叫聲在三年以前	in fact , when you're eating lunch on sunday , you're likely to hear the sounds of the cow outside the window three years ago .
因此 , 顯然他是一個有機城市屬於有機迴圈中的一個部分	so , obviously , he's part of an organic city , part of an organic loop .
但是 , 10年後 , 一切都改變了	but after 10 years , everything changed .
這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is a photograph of the great western railway in 1840 .
你可以看見 , 一些早期的鐵路乘客們是豬和羊群	as you can see , some early railroad passengers were pigs and sheep .
一夕之間 , 這些動物不再走進市場	all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into the market .
他們被屠宰了在鄉村的某個地方	they've been slaughtered somewhere in the countryside .
然後他們透過鐵路來到了城市	and they came to the city through the railroad .
這些改變了一切	and that changed everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first of all , he had the first time that cities were growing into cities wherever they were , what size and shapes they were .
城市發展過去受到地理的限制城市需要透過很艱難的方式獲得食物	cities have developed past constraints in geography , and cities need to get food in a tough way .
突然 , 他們從地理限制中解放了出來	all of a sudden , they liberated from geography .
你可以看看倫敦的地圖在鐵路建成後的90年它從容易餵飽的一小點透過動物步行到市場等方式成長成為大型的奢侈的大都市步行運輸再也不能餵飽每個人不論是對人還是對動物	if you look at the map of london in the 90 years after the railroad was made , it went from a small dot that was easy to feed , and it grew up in large luxury of urban walks and urban walks and transportation , and it wouldn't feed everyone , whether it's right or for animals .
當然 , 這僅僅是開始 。 當汽車代替了火車這真正標誌這個過程的結束	and of course , it's just the beginning . when the car substitutes the train , it's really the end of the process .
這是城市的最終解放從自然的束縛中完全的解放了	it's the final liberation of the city from the constraints of nature , completely liberated .
這樣型別的城市沒有了原來城市的味道亂糟糟的市容 , 當然也缺少了人因為沒有人想要在這麼大的一塊地方步行	it doesn't have the smell of the original city , and of course it's missing because nobody wants to walk in such a big place .
事實上 , 他們都開小汽車去購買食物了開車去郊外的超級市場買回來一週需要的食物然後考慮到底如何規劃這些食品	in fact , they're all driving cars to buy food , driving to the rural supermarkets , buying food for a week , and thinking about how to actually plan these foods .
這時刻 , 食物和城市的關係 , 完全的改變了	at this point , the relationship between food and urban is completely changed .
過去買食物是在市中心在城市的最核心地帶	it used to be that we bought food in the central part of the city .
買賣食物曾經是一種社會性的活動 ,	buying food was a social activity .
我們原來還需要烹飪 , 現在我們只需要加水或者是一些雞蛋 , 當我們在做蛋糕或者其他東西的時候	it turns out we need to cook . we need to add water or some eggs when we're making cake or something .
我們不會在去聞聞食物來確認它是否可以吃了	we're not going to smell food to identify if it's going to eat .
我們只是閱讀包裝袋上的使用說明就好	we're just reading the instructions on the packages .
我們沒有發現食物的價值 , 我們也不信賴它	we don't discover the value of food , and we don't trust it .
我們甚至擔心它	we're even worried about it .
從體會它的價值變成浪費	from recognizing its value to wasting .
當今食品工業最最諷刺的是他們讓生活極致地便利卻也使得一切更為複雜	the irony of today's food industry is that they've made it extremely convenient , but they've made it even more complicated .
因為可以自由的建立新城市但是他們卻疏遠了人可貴的聯絡也就是人與自然的聯絡	because they're free to build new cities , but they're removed from the expensive contact of people and nature .
同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴這個系統這個系統 , 在我們看來 , 是不可持續的	at the same time , they also allow us to rely on this system , which is unsustainable , in our opinion .

這不是一個新的問題	it's not a new question .

它是一個半獨立的城邦如果這麼說聽上去還比較熟悉的話一天的行走你會看見所有人農場都在瘋狂的種植或者在自己的後院種植蔬菜然後一起享用鄉鎮的共有食物 , 等等	it's a semiindependent citystate , and if that sounds more familiar to walk on a day , you're going to see all the farms growing in crazy , or growing vegetables in their own backyard , and sharing shared food with the town , and so on .
