當仁愛憲章發起數星期後 , 卡倫•阿姆斯特朗又將目光轉向宗教在二十一世紀所扮演的角色 。 她提出: " 宗教教義是否會使我們產生分歧 ? 抑或將我們團結在一起為了共同的利益 ? " 她回顧了能帶動全球信仰重拾恕道的催化劑 。	when the charter of compassion started a few weeks later , karen armstrom looked at the role of religion in the 21st century , and she said , " is religious doctrines going to divide us , or is it going to bring us together in solidarity for common good ? " she looked back at catalysts that drive global faith .
god , tedprize , globalissues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	you know , ted prize , global isisues , politics , religion , tedglobal , 2009 , violence .
卡倫•阿姆斯特朗:重拾恕道	karen armsterram: reclaim forgiveness .
多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪因為作為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經意識到世界上主要的宗教信仰都宣揚仁愛之心 。	for years , i've been frustrated because as a religious historian , i've realized that the majority of the world's religious beliefs proclaimed compassion .
每個宗教都演變出自己獨特的版本 , 這些統稱為恕道 。	each religion has evolved its own unique version of its own , and these statistics are called forgive
有時從正面說 , 那就是- " 推己及人 。 "	sometimes it's , from the front , that's " selfmotivating . "
同樣重要的 , 從反方面說就是-- " 已所不欲 , 勿施於人 。 "	and equally important , in the opposite direction , it's " don't do to humans . "
審視你的內心 。 探尋究竟是什麼讓你痛苦 。 然後在任何情況下 , 都拒絕將這種痛苦施加於別人 。	scrutinize your heart , seek out what causes you to suffer , and in any case , refuse to apply that pain to others .
人們之所以重視仁愛 , 不僅僅是因為它聽起來很棒 , 更是因為它行得通 。	and the reason why people value compassion is not just because it sounds great , but because it works .
人們發現當他們遵守恕道時正如孔子所說的 " 終生行之 , " 這已不是隻做一天好事然後又回到貪婪、自私的生活的問題了 。 當你每天都堅守恕道的時候 , 你就可以擺脫以自我為中心的世界 , 超然於物外 。	people find that when they follow the purpose of forgiveness , as confucius says , " lifelong , " this is not a matter of doing a good day and then returning to greed and having a life of selfishness , and when you hold onto a daily basis , you can get out of the world of selfcenteredness and beyond that .
從而可以到達稱之為神、涅盤、喇嘛、道的境界 。	it gets to what's called god , nirvana , lama , lama .
一些超越我們所知的自我約束的東西 。	something beyond what we know about ourselves .
但是 , 你知道大多數時候你對此一無所知 , 這就是宗教生活的核心 。	but , you know , most of the time you don't know anything about it , and that's the core of religious life .
因為世上的一些特例 , 經常的 , 當宗教人士集聚在一起的時候 , 宗教領袖聚在一起的時候 , 他們會爭辯深奧的理論或者發表充滿仇恨的言論又或譴責同性戀等此類問題 。	because the unusual exceptions of the world , often , when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they argue about the esoteric theory or publish hateful speech or denounce homosexuality and so on .
通常人們不具有仁愛之心 。	people don't usually have compassion .
有時 , 當我跟眾多宗教人士交談時 , 我注意到他們的臉上經常會閃現一絲輕蔑之色 , 因為人們往往都自持正確 。	sometimes when i talk to many religious people , i notice that their faces often appear contemporary because they tend to be true .
這當然違背了修行的目的 。	of course , it's a violation of purpose .

因為ted溫柔地將我從滿是書本的書房帶到了二十一世紀 , 讓我能夠可以向更多 , 更廣的觀眾演說這比我能設想到的多得多 。	because ted gently brought me from a room full of books and into the 21st century , allowing me to speak much more to a wider audience than i could ever have dreamed of .

假若我們不設法在全球實施恕道 , 這樣我們就能對待所有的人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 他們是誰 , 都如同對待我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們能否將這個世界傳承給下一代 。	if we don't manage to implement forgiveness globally so that we can treat everyone , wherever they are , as important as ourselves , and i wonder if we can pass this world to the next generation .
我們當前的任務 , 最為艱鉅的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 就像我所說的 , 在這個社會里 , 人們可以和諧相處 。	one of the toughest missions of our time is to build a global society , as i say , in this society , where people can relate to each other .

馬來西亞將會舉辦一場藝術展覽 , 屆時 , 頂尖的畫家們將會帶領人們 , 年青的一代 , 展示給他們仁愛也根植於所有的藝術中 。	malaysia is going to have an art exhibition , and then the top painters will lead people , the young ones , showing them that kindness is rooted in all art .

要教育 。 因為我們如此地遠離了仁愛 。	education , because we're moving away from compassion .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	the mit researcher , skyla tibiz , who works on selfassembly a project where instead of building things , we can create materials that are very much like the dna chain packing , and so far it's an early stage of an enormous concept , where tibiz shows us three projects that are still there , and we can peer into the possibility of a selfassembly future .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	sk: can we make things that we can make ourselves ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	i'd like to show you today how we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe that soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplication and selfrepair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think is the manufacturing industry , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have skyscrapers two and a half years , 500 , 000 to million parts , very complicated using new technologies for steel and concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that can fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , and we can restore that in about one hour with three billion base pairs of pairs of dna .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	this is the complexity of our natural systems , but they're very efficient , more efficient than anything we build , more complicated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more efficient on energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they don't make much mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can selfrepair longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	it's a fascinating thing about natural systems .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert it into our architectural environment , then there's a huge potential for how we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to harness selfassembly in our own bodies , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexity of what we're building , our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences that are essentially the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need the programmable parts to accept that sequence and to fold or reconstruct it .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to start , so that our parts can fold in according to the program .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some kind of error correct redundancy to guarantee that what we're building is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to make this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are all reconfigurable robots eight feet , 12 feet long proteins .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in mechanical electrical devices , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you need to decode the way you want to fold into a series of angles minus 120 degrees , negative 120 degrees , zero degrees , zero degrees , 120 degrees , etc . , a series of angles , or shifts , to get this sequence through .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit takes its own message , like minus 120 , and it rotates , checks if it spins to its neighbors .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there's a lot of brilliant scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think the project really reveals: is this really scalable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it cost thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand it ? can we really embed robots in every part ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next problem is looking at passiveity , or passively trying to make reconfiguration programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it goes a little further , and it tries to actually compute .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	it basically embeds most computational building blocks , digital logic gates , directly into all parts .
這是與非門 。	it's not a gatekeeper .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each of these doors has a tetrahedron on the calculation door , which has two inputs .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one of them is the input from the user , just like you're building blocks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other is a brick input that was previously introduced .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it's going to give the threedimensional export .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that the users build bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates based on previous instructions and your commands .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it's starting to move up or down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , and it goes down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , 0] input is one output , expressing upwards .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structures now contain blueprints that we want to build .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about the things that want to construct is embedded .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	it means that we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call it selfdirected copying , because your structure contains accurate blueprints .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if there's a mistake , you can replace parts .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	local information is embedded in , telling you how to repair it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that can climb and read and output one way .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's directly embedded ; there's no external input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show you is called the paranoid chain , and it's probably the most exciting example of the passive selfassembly system that we're seeing right now .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reconstructability and programmability that makes it a system for completely passive systems .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	it's basically a series of elements that you have .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is completely identical , and they're preferred .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each strand , or each element wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want to assemble a chain , you need to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	tell each element to turn left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	and when you shake this chain , it folds up , and it programs whatever structure you code , so in this case , a helix , fire , and in this case , two cubes that are connected .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	you can basically program it in three dimensions , or in one dimension , or two dimensions it's completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what kind of future does this tell us about ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think what this tells us is the possibility of selfassembly , selfreplication and selfrepair in our bodies , our buildings and machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	and in those sections , there's new programmability .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you can get the new possibilities of computation .
我們將有空間計算 。	we're going to have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines , all the bricks can actually compute .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing parallel computing and distributed computing power and new design possibilities .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	and i think these projects that i've shown you are just a tiny step towards the future , if we can build these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've stepped on to the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even been to the deepest of the sea twice twice . what's left to explore ? biologists and nathan wolf asks the answer: almost everything . " we can start from that tiny little to the world , " he says .
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	bioversity , you name it , biology .
內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼值得探索 ?	nathan wolf: what's worth exploring ?
最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i recently went to berroy , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to honor a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions for the unknown , such as the gobi beach .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he was an incredible figure .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	he later said it was the indiana jones character prototype .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in burroyt , wisconsin , i gave a bunch of high school students a public class .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	i'd like to tell you now that if it's harder to do a ted talk , it's trying to keep their attention a thousand 12yearolds and stay for 45 minutes .
在我講完之後 , 他們問了很多問題 , 但有一個讓我自始至終難以忘記 。	after my talk , they asked a lot of questions , but one of them made me never forget .
有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	a little girl stood up and asked a question: " where should we explore ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think the vast majority of our notions are that the age of exploration on earth is over , and our next generation should go to outer space or the deepest of the oceans to find things worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that true ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	isn't it really important for us to explore ? there's none of it all over the planet ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	it reminds me of one of my favorite explorers in biology .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he's an explorer of the unknown world , martin nus william lyellerk .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	and byelink , who was trying to figure out what caused the tobacco lesion .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he extracted infected tobacco sap , and he let the sap through a much more thin layer of filter than a layer of infection .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	he came to the conclusion that there must be something left out there that is smaller than the smallest known life form of bacteria , bacteria .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he gives this mysterious thing a name .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	call them viruses in latin for " poisonous . "
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after discovering the virus , eric opened a whole new world for us .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other life .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and it's clear that there's been an enormous number of incisions that have been used in viruses such as the eradication of smallpox , the decline of vaccines in utero that we now know are mostly caused by sarcoma viruses .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and byeller's discovery was not 500 years ago .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	byeller found out that the virus was happening more than 100 years ago .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	that means that when the cars have been around , we don't yet know that they've made most of the genetic information on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some amazing tools to help us explore the unknown , like the genetic deep sequencing , that allow us not just to remain on the surface to look at the independent genomes of a particular species , but to study the entire genome the microbial community in our bodies and around us , and to document the genetic information of these species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these technologies to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my institutions , we do this all the time to find the causes of riots , the reasons why we don't know .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine taking a nasal secretion specimen from each of you .
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	things like this are things we do all the time to find respiratory viruses , like flu .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	so the first thing we're looking at is the amount of genetic information that's inherited .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at these genetic information , we're going to see some common information , and of course , a lot of human genetic information , but a lot of bacteria and viruses , mostly harmless things in your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we'll also see some very , very surprising things .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	and when we started looking at this information , we found that 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose was informed by anything that we've seen any plant , animal , fungi or bacteria .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we basically don't know anything about these things .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small percentage of the people that we're working on this data are called biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we know we've never seen these biological dark matters before ; it seems to be the unknown continent in our own genetic information .
而且數量非常之多 。	and there's a lot of it .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think that 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , then when we look at your internal organs , it's almost 40 to 50 percent biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in relatively sterile blood , one to two percent of the information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be categorized , can't be categorized , can't be determined what we've seen .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	at first we thought it was manmade .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these genetic deep sequencing tools are quite new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they get more and more accurate , we think that information is a new form of life , or at least a part of it , is a form of life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	and even these assumptions about explaining the existence of biological dark matter are still in the infancy , a very , very exciting possibility exists: hiding within this life , there's a marker of life that isn't recognized by genetic information .
當我們探索這些一串串a/t/c/g嘌呤的時候 , 我們也許會發現全新的生命 , 就像拜耶林克 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學特性的理解 。	and as we explore these cascades of a/t/ghour purineines , we may find entirely new life , like byelink , fundamentally changing our understanding of biology .
這也許會讓我識別出困擾我們的某種癌症的原因 , 或者識別出我們不熟悉的疾病暴發的根源 , 或者創造出一種分子生物學的新工具 。	it may recognize the causes of some type of cancer that troubles us , or the root causes of a disease atrocity that we're not familiar with or the new tools of molecular biology .
我很高興的宣佈 , 和我的斯坦福、加州理工和舊金山加利福尼亞大學的同事們一起 , 我們正在開始開始一個新的行動去探索生物暗物質來尋找新生命的存在 。	i'm pleased to announce that with my stanford and caltech and colleagues at the university of california , we're beginning a new action to explore the existence of biological dark matter .
100多年前 , 人們還不知道病毒的存在 , 這些包含我們星球上大部分遺傳資訊的生命形態 。	more than a hundred years ago , people had no idea that viruses existed , including most of the genetic information on our planet .
一百年以後 , 人類可能為我們以前完全不瞭解的新的生命形態而感到驚訝而它們就在我們眼皮底下 。	a hundred years later , humans may be surprised by a new form of life that we've never understood before , and they're under our eyes .
沒錯 , 我們或許已經繪製這個星球上所有大陸板塊的地圖 , 我們或許已經發現了當前所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不代表地球上沒什麼好探索的了 。	yes , we've probably mapped all of the continental plates on the planet , and we've probably discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing to explore on earth .
拜耶林克和像他一樣的人們給下一代探索者上了重要的一課----給那些像那個在伯洛伊特市的女孩一樣的人們 。	byeller and others like him have given us a very important lesson to the next generation of explorers to the same people like that girl in berroet .
我想如果總結一下他給我們上的這一課 , 大概是:不要假設我們現在想到的東西是一個完整的故事 。	and i think if you summarize the lesson that he's given to us , it's like , don't assume that what we're thinking about now is a complete story .
在不管你選擇的任何領域裡去探索那些暗物質吧 。	explore those dark matter in whatever area you're choosing .
未知的事物在我們身邊無處不在它們只是在等待人類的探索 。	the unknown things are everywhere around us , they're just waiting for human discovery .

隨後密集的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用 。 其中一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式逃離 , 照亮了宏偉的太空 , --我認為相當於一千億個太陽的光亮 。	subsequent magnetic fields directed some of the energy in the gravitational collapse , and some of the matter escaped in the form of giant jets and illuminated the spectacular space , which i think is the equivalent of 100 billion suns .
然而 , 與這樣一個噴射流的物理相比 , 我們人類大腦的物理大相徑庭到極點 。	however , compared to the physics of a jet like this , the physics of our human brain is extremely different .
在這樣的環境裡 , 我們連一瞬間都無法生存 。 當我們試著描述那樣的噴射流中的狀況 , 語言變得無法表達 。	in such environments , we can't survive instantaneously , and when we try to describe the conditions of that jet , language becomes impossible to express .
這可能有點像經歷一次超新星爆炸 , 但是是在零距離接觸並且將數百萬年的能量集中到同一時間爆發 。	it's a bit like going through a supernova explosion , but at zero distances and concentrating millions of years of energy at the same time .

一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另外一個物理系統的準確工作模型--類星體 。	a physics system , the brain , contains the accurate working model of the other physics system the celestial star .
不僅僅是一個粗淺的影象 , 雖然也包含影象 , 而且還包含解釋性的模型 , 表達同樣的數學關係和一樣的因果結構 。	it's not just a shallow imaging , it's also an image , it's also an explanatory model that expresses the same mathematical relations and the same causal structure .
這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠讓你驚訝的話 , 一個結構表達另外一個的準確性正隨著時間不斷提高 。 這就是知識的增長 。	that's the knowledge . if that's not enough to surprise you , the structure expresses another accuracy over time . that's the growth of knowledge .
因此 , 物理規律擁有這樣一個特殊的性質 。	so , the laws of physics have this special property .
物體 , 不管他們彼此多麼相異 , 卻仍然能夠表現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間增長表現得越來越多 。	objects , no matter how different they are , can still behave the same mathematical and causal structures , and they can behave more and more over time .
因此我們是與眾不同的化學汙垢 。 這一化學汙垢擁有普適性 。	so we're remarkably different chemical scaling . this chemical scum has adaptability .
它的結構準確度越來越高地包容著 , 世界萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙中任何其他地方 , 在它自身內部 , 成為一個包容了其他一切宇宙萬物結構性和因果性精髓的中心 。 因此 , 意義深遠的是 , 物理規律允許這一現象 , 抑或甚至主導了它的發生這一事實是關於物理世界的最重要的事情之一 。	its structure is getting more accurate , more accurate , more accurate , more accurately , the structure of the world , not anywhere else in the universe , becoming at the center of all the rest of the universe's structural and causal essence , so the really profound thing is that the laws of physics allow this physics , or even dominate its physics , one of the most important things about the physical world .
那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	so how does the solar system how does our environment , in our form , get a special relationship to the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	now , stephen hawking was accurate i mean , it's true , but it's wrong . one of the accurate aspects of it is that it doesn't rely on any special physics . there's no special enrichment , no miracles , and it only depends only on the three things that we're wearing now .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing , information processing requires computation , computing requires computers no matter whatsoever to make computers .
我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要使得用來記錄我們所發現知識的媒介工作 。	we also need energy to make computers , and most importantly , to keep the media that we've discovered sources of knowledge .
第三種東西 , 較難感觸得到 , 但是在開放式的知識和解釋的開發中同樣關鍵的是證據 。	the third thing is harder to reach , but the same crucial evidence in openended knowledge and explanation is evidence .
我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is filled with evidence .
但是我們常常忽略了測試--比如 , 牛頓的地球引力定律--大約是在300年前提出的 。	but we often ignore tests things like newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .
但是我們習以為常的證據 , 從數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在接下來的數十億年裡繼續墜落 。 其他科學也同樣如此 。	but the evidence that we've been used to , which has been falling down in every corner of the earth for billions of years , has been falling on for the next billion years as well as others .
就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學大部分基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上等待我們獲取 。	as far as we know , the evidence to discover most fundamental truths in science is just waiting for us on our planet .
我們所在的地方充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。	where we are is filled with evidence , with matter and energy .
而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic space , those three premises to create openended knowledge are extremely small .
正如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 黑暗 。 抑或不是如此 ?	as i said , there's nothing there , it's cold , it's dark , or not ?
事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。	in fact , it's just another narrow misunderstanding .
假想在星系間空間有一個立方體存在 , 與我們的房屋般大小 , 太陽系 。 以我們的標準來看 , 這個立方體非常空 , 但是它事實上仍然包含著超過百萬噸的物質 。	imagine that there's a cube in intergalactic space the size of our houses , the solar system , and in our standards , it's a very empty cube , but it actually contains over a million tons of matter .
一百萬噸足夠建造一個 , 比方說 , 自給自足的空間站 , 在這個空間站內聚居著一群科學家 , 他們致力於不斷創造開放式的知識 , 等等 。	a million tons of construction is enough to build , say , a selfsufficient space station that gathers around the space station a group of scientists who are working to create open knowledge and so on .
然而 , 現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成別的元素等都遠不能做到 。	however , even today's technologies can't even capture hydrogen from intergalactic space and convert it into other elements .
但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in an understandable universe , if something is permitted by the laws of physics , then what's going to prevent us from doing it ?
換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and if we can do that , then we'll automatically get energy supply , because what's going to change here is the nuclear reaction evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	again , it's dark for human senses , but what you need to do is pick up a telescope , even today's technology , and look out , and you'll see the same galaxies that we see from here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a stronger telescope , you'll see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics , you can study the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	in your position , you can make particle accelerators , you can study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the hardest science to do is biology field trips , because it takes millions of years to return to the nearest living planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you sorry , richard but i never really liked biology field trips so much , i think we can just do it every million years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so in fact , intergalactic space isn't the premise of an openended creation of knowledge , and any cube like this can be the same center anywhere in the universe , if the knowledge of this project exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only places to be passionate .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic spaces can create an opensource channel , it's almost everywhere else , and the earth is the same as the earth .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factors , and there , are not resources , because resources are plentiful , but knowledge , scarcity .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	this cosmic view of knowledge perhaps i think it should make us feel very extraordinary , but it also makes us feel our vulnerability , because it means that without the specific needs of our knowledge to help us deal with the challenges of sources in the universe , we will not survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	just one supernova explosion just a few lightyears away , and we will all be dead .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees recently wrote a book about our vulnerability to all things , from astrophysics to scientific experiments , and most importantly , the terrorism of weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he thought that human civilization only has a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he's going to talk about it later at this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think that's the probability to describe this problem .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him that we can survive , and we may not survive either .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , it's whether we're able to create knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	this danger is certainly not unprecedented . species are always extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations will end . the vast majority of species and civilizations exist in history .

如果你想在一個村莊改變體制 , 可以 , 但一個村的規模太小了不能帶給你如同讓百萬人一樣的效應在優質體制的治理下	if you want to change the system in a village , yes , but the scale of a village is too small to give you the same effect that millions of people have in the superior system .
另一方面 , 一下子改變全國的體制又太大了	on the other hand , the systems that change the country are too large .
如果你想改變國家體制有一部分人必然得不到照顧他們也沒有機會去評估新政的優劣給人民一個聚焦未來 , 嘗試新體制的機會	if you want to change the system , there's a certain amount of people who don't have access to care , and they don't have the opportunity to assess the strengths of a new regime , to focus on the future , to try a new system .
但像城市就能給你這些機會來建立新領域開拓新體制 , 人們可以選擇	but cities like this can give you these opportunities to build new frontiers , to open up new institutions , people can choose .
並且足夠大大到我們能得到應有的當百萬人在新體制治理下應有的效應	and it's big enough to get the millions of people that are supposed to have effects in new systems of governance .
所以我提議我們設想一種叫做 " 特別市 " 的東西	so i propose that we think about something called " special markets . "
首先綱領詳細說明所有的條例規則來吸引那些建設特別市的人才	the first syllabus details all the rules to attract those who build special markets .
我們需要吸引投資商他們會建設基礎設施能源系統 , 公路 , 碼頭 , 機場 , 樓房	we need to attract investors , and they'll build infrastructure infrastructure , energy systems , roads , yards , airports , buildings .
你需要吸引商家他們會來聘用最先移居特別市的人們	you need to attract merchants who are going to hire the first people to migrate from the city .
你需要吸引家庭那些會來長期居住的人撫養小孩 , 供他們受教育開始他們的事業	you need to attract families , those who come and live longterm , raise children , to start educating them , to start their business .
在這樣的綱領下 , 人們會移居那裡	and under those syllabuses , people moved there .
城市才能建立起來	it's the ability to build cities .
我們還可以改善這個模型的規模	we can also improve the scale of the model .
我們可以一遍又一遍地	we can do it over and over again .
要想成功 , 我們需要完善地體制 。 我們已經討論過了	to succeed , we need to have perfect systems . we've discussed them .
這些將在綱領中體現出來	these are going to be embodied in syllabus .
我們還需要給人們自由去選擇	we also need to give people the freedom to choose .
是真正融入了這個模型如果我們允許在無人居住的土地上建設城市的話	it's a model that really integrates into the model if we allow cities to be built on uninhabited land .
你從荒蕪的領地開始	you start with the desolate territory .
人們可以移居那裡開始新的綱領但沒有人是被迫的	people could remove from there to start their new syllabus , but nobody was forced to do it .
最後 , 我們需要給領導者自由去選擇	finally , we need to give leaders the freedom to choose .
要做到給領導者自由我們需要允許國家間的合作讓不同的國家可以合作事實上像中國和英國合作一樣來首先建設一個市場經濟的飛地然後擴大至整個中國	to do that , to give freedom to leaders , we need to allow countries to work together so that they can actually , like china and the uk , build a market economy for the first time and scale up to china .
或多或少 , 英國 , 不經意地在上個世紀它治理香港期間對削減世界貧困上做出了比任何支援專案都更為卓越的貢獻	more or less , britain inadvertently , in the last century , it ran an even greater contribution to reducing world poverty than any support project .
所以只要我們允許這樣的合作重演我們可以將這個效應擴大的整個世界的規模	so if we allow this kind of collaboration to reproduce , we can scale this across the world .
有時這需要委派職責一種從一個國家到另外一個國家的責任的委派來執行某些行政管理的職責	sometimes it takes a duty of commission , a duty of responsibility from one country to another , to run some administrative accountability .
我這麼說你們中有些人可能開始想 " 那 , 不是要恢復殖民主義嗎 ? "	i say that some of you are probably starting to think , " well , isn't it reclaiming colonialism ? "
不是的 。 但是認識到這種情緒卻是重要的我們開始考慮這些時 , 這些情緒將產生會阻礙我們扼殺我們的能力我們探索新想法的興趣	no . but recognizing that emotion is important , and when we think about it , these emotions are going to stifle our capabilities , and we're interested in exploring new ideas .
為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?	why isn't that colonialism ?
殖民主義的弊病以及支援專案遺留的弊端是它具有強迫和屈尊的元素	the illness of colonialism and the cheating of support projects is elements of force and respect .
但模型的核心是自由選擇無論是對領導者來說 , 還是對來移居的人民來說	but at the heart of the model is free choice , both for leaders and for migrants .
這自由選擇恰恰正是強迫和屈尊的解藥	the freedom option is exactly the antidote to force and respect .

管理一個特別的行政區	a special administration district .

非洲 。 我曾和非洲的領導者溝透過	africa . i talked to african leaders .

從艱苦漫長的環球探險中 , 基因組學先驅克雷格•文特忙裡偷閒 , 為我們講述其團隊描繪海洋生物多樣性的歷程 。 到目前為止 , 他們已經發現了數百萬的基因 。	from a very long , long global adventure , genomic pioneer craig venter was busy describing the diversity of marine biodiversity for our team , and so far , they've found millions of genes .
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , welcome , marion .
克雷格•文特:dna和海洋	craig venter: dna and the ocean .
休息的時候 , 有幾個人過來問我對老齡化問題怎麼看	at rest , a couple of people came up and asked me what i thought about aging .
我的唯一看法是	and the only way i think about it is this .
我認為樂觀主義者比悲觀主義者活得久得多	i think optimists live a lot longer than pessimists .
在這18分鐘裡我將告訴你們的是我們是如何做到從最初的閱讀遺傳編碼發展到我們自己開始編寫遺傳編碼	what i'm going to tell you about in those 18 minutes is how we've moved from reading genetic code to encoding ourselves .
僅僅十年之前的這個月我們發表了第一個來自自由活動生命體的基因序列即流感嗜血桿菌的序列	only a decade ago this month , we published the first genome sequence of free activity , the sequence of haemophilus .
由此我們將基因組專案完成的時間從13年降到4個月	so we've gone from 13 years to four months by genomic projects .
現在 , 同樣的基因組專案只需要2到8個小時	now , the same genome project only takes two to eight hours .
因此過去十年 , 我們完成了大量的基因組測序大部分的人類病原體幾種植物多種昆蟲和哺乳動物包括人類基因組	so over the last 10 years , we've done a lot of sequencing genomes , most of the human pathogens , several plants , multiple insects and mammals ,
約在十年前我們對基因組學發展的設想是到今年年底的時候我們或許能完成3到5個基因組的測序而事實上已經完成了數百個	about a decade ago , the idea of genomics was that by the end of this year , we might be able to sequence three to five genomes , and in fact , hundreds of them have been completed .
我們剛剛從戈登-貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得一筆資助作為環境有機體專案的副專案我們將在今年完成130個基因組的測序	we just got a funding project from gordon betty moore foundation to do the environmental organism project , and we're going to sequence 130 genomes this year .
閱讀遺傳編碼的速率已然改變	the rate of reading genetic code has changed .
但我們看到 , 未來的路還很長我們僅僅探索了這個星球表面上淺淺的一層	but we see that the future is long , and we've only explored its shallow surfaces .
大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most of us don't realize that these invisible microbes make up about half of the biomass on earth , and all animals add up to a thousandth of the biomass of the earth .
跑到海邊喝上一口海水或許不是牛津人經常做的事但請記住每一毫升的海水裡有大約一百萬個的細菌其中的病毒更是以千萬計	go to the beach and drink a bite of seawater , maybe not something that oxfords do regularly , but keep in mind that every millililiter of seawater has about a million bacteria , and that virus is tens of millions of viruses .
兩年前只有不到五千種的微生物被鑑定歸類於是我們決定做些這方面的事情	less than 5 , 000 microbes were identified two years ago , so we decided to do something about it .
我們啟動了巫師二號考察和其他大型的海洋考察活動一樣我們嘗試每200英里採一次樣	we started a shaman ii expedition , like any big ocean expedition , and we tried to take a sample every 200 miles .
考察伊始 , 我們在百慕大進行了測試專案然後前往哈利法克斯接著到美國東海岸加勒比海、巴拿馬運河穿過加拉帕哥斯群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋現在我們正在穿越印度洋的過程中	we tested it in bermuda , and then we went to halifax , and we went to the east coast of the united states , the caribbean , the panama canal , through the galapagos and across the pacific , and now we're in the process of going across the indian ocean .
工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's hard work . we're taking a sailing boat , and in a way we're interested in getting young people into science .
實驗其實非常簡單	it's a very simple experiment .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	we take seawater , we filter it with different filters , we take different size organisms and we take their dna back to rokwell's lab , where we can measure 100 million cross genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and through that , we've made some surprising discoveries .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , before our eyes , pigment is thought that only one or two organisms in nature have the same pigments as us .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the upper regions of the warm sea , almost every species has this kind of light receptor , and they use sunlight as a source and communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	just one point , from one barrel of water , we can see that 13 million new genes are equivalent to 50 , 000 new ones .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	by funding from the sloan foundation , we've expanded our research into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how many viruses and bacteria are floating in the air we breathe every day , especially in closed environments like airplanes and auditoriums .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we filtered billions of microorganisms on the top of a building in new york city just a day , and we filtered billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're doing sequencing right now .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	just from the dataset , just from the galapagos islands , we've discovered that for almost 200 miles , we've been able to see enormous diversity in the sample collection .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	different temperature gradients may be explaining some of this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite based on temperature , showing warm areas in red , cool areas in blue , and what we found was that samples and samples in warm seas are very different in the richness of the species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	another surprising thing for us is that these receptors can detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict this process through their amino acid sequences .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	they're enormous in different regions .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	it's probably not surprising that it's almost ghostly deep in the deep sea , receptors tend to look at it to blue .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	and while traveling towards the extreme infrared and the ultraviolet period , the light receptors may be even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	to assess all the genes that we've been collecting , we've collected all the data , including all the data that we've been testing so far represents more than half of the genetic data on earth .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we put these genes into the genomic family , trying to answer: are we finding new members of the known genomic families , or are we discovering new gene family members ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out that we've found about 50 , 000 primary gene family members , but every new sample that we've obtained from the environment is simply a linear address for these new genomic families .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the earliest stages of discovery of life on earth and its parts and genetic basis .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	let's look at the socalled evolutionary tree , and we humans are in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	we only have 24 , 000 genes in the animal kingdom .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we count all the animals together , we're sharing with them less than 3 , 000 , maybe at 120 , 000 , or more thousands of different genetic families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now i'm not just going to think of these genes as design components of evolution .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go back to richard dawkins's theory of genomecentric view , rather than the " genomecentric view " to think about how they're made of these genetic components differently .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has been in sync with dna sequencing over the last 10 or 20 years , in a way that has been increasingly syncing rapidly and cheaper .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea about synthetic genomics was that in 1995 , we thought about the second genitalia , which is the sequencing of the genitalia .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty good tshirt that says , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's actually just a tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	it has almost 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we asked if one species needed 800 genes , the other 500 genes , to be able to make a tiny , tiny operating system out of a smaller set of genome .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started changing the seat mutation .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the transmitter is short pieces of dna that randomly inserts into the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert a seat into the gene , it disrupts the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so what we've done is we've identified all the genes that can be inserted into these transfers , and we've combined that we don't necessarily need to make a map .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environment is crucial for this , and we can only define the need and nonnecessary genes based on the conditions that actually exist in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to do a more intuitive study of 13 related creatures , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they had the same thing .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found out that only 173 of them are the same in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if you ignore a parasite in a cell , this genetic bank expands a little bit , and when we look at a set of 310 genes , the gene pool expands even more .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we think we can expand from the minimum 500 genes , or shrink down , how do you think about this problem , to something like 300 to 400 genes ?
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to build a chromosome out of these genes , and we have to do it based on expressing the frame .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	and what we found was that large pieces of synthetic dna were very , very difficult to do .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague han smith and clay hutchinson have invented an exciting new way that we can synthesize a virus with 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , 100 percent accurate in gene sequence and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a pretty exciting experiment: we just injected synthetic dna fragments into bacteria , and suddenly the dna started to guide the synthesis of virus particles , and viruses came back and killed bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	it's not the first synthetic virus that's been produced a year ago , but it's the only one percent of active viruses take three years to synthesize .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is an animation of the phix174 structure .
這是軟體為自己構建硬體的活例子也為我們的生物學提供了新想法	this is a living example of the software that built its own hardware and provided new ideas for our biology .
有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	immediately , i was worried about the threat of biological weapons , and a while ago , i was at the senate committee and another special committee of the u . s . government aimed to testify in this field .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think the most important thing is to keep facts in mind , not people's imaginations about things .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	essentially , any virus that's been sequenced now can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were terrified by things like the ebola virus or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not contagious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if you're a smallpox virus , the dna itself doesn't cause infections .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security sector really needs to worry about designer viruses .
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union have been working on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if these studies have actually ended , the probability of designing viruses in the future is very , very small .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible in two years to make singlecelled organisms .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the real nuclear cells , the kinds of cells we have , can be made in a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can distinguish between the different expression of the artificial genome and the different genes that allow us to build dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	the key is , how do you put all the rest in ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	so we're going to start with these clips , and then we're going to start with a homologous recombination of them into a chromosome .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from a creature called deinococcus radiodurans that remains alive under three million radical doses of radiation .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in exposure to exposure for about 12 to 24 hours , the chromosome is almost completely broken , and it can also reassemble its own chromosomes .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	these organisms are virtually everywhere on earth , and even because of human activity , they're probably out there in space .
這是玻璃燒杯在約50萬拉德輻射下的情形	this is a glass burning glass , about half a million radical radiation .
玻璃開始燃燒 , 爆裂而位於底部的微生物則似乎越來越開心	glass starts to burn , burns , and the microbes on the bottom seem to be getting happier and happier .
這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	this is actually what happens with chromosomes after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it's almost been broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	and the bottom is after 24 hours of the same dna automatically recombined .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	and these organisms are really marvelous . if it's not tens of thousands , maybe we'll be able to find thousands and thousands of other species , we'll be able to do the same .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	the first step after these genomes are transplanted into cells that have no genome .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think that synthetic cells are going to have a tremendous promise , not just for understanding biology , but for the environmental and social problems that are going to help us deal with .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for instance , from the third species that we sequenced , methane bacteria lived at the equivalent of hydrogen boiling at high temperatures in the water boiling and relied on capturing carbon dioxide in the environment .
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	and it turns out that thousands of creatures can capture and rely on carbon dioxide in a vast variety of different ways .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can replace the carbon products that are made from the atmosphere by capturing carbon in the atmosphere or other products that are made from oil industry .
有種依賴一氧化碳的生物我們利用其還原能力使水分子破裂 , 製造出氫和氧	there's a species that depend on carbon dioxide , and we're using its ability to crack the water molecules and make hydrogen
同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many other ways to translate methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	one of the big projects the dupont and norwegian oil companies have converted methane into useful products in norway's oil fields .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it struck me that there was a new field called combinatoric genomics that was going to be born very quickly , because with these new methods of synthesis , there was this huge genome sequence and same recombination , we could design a robot that could produce almost a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so all the biology features can be selected through screens , whether it's manufacturing hydrogen chemicals , or it's just survival .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	understanding how these genes are going to be doing is going to be able to reach their hands .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis is oxygenregulated , and the hydrogeninsensitive enzymes that we use are completely different .
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrated multiple cellular enzymes , and these enzymes could take complex sugar categories and make alcohol in the same cell .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	and in some big labs , we're starting to use microbes to do drug production .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemistry of the environmental compounds is much more complex than the chemical compounds that our best chemists have built .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps the future engineering species will be our food source , our energy source , our environmental rescue , and even replace the fossil industry .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me finish with morality and policy research .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	we late to the 1999 experiment , until the question of whether we should try to make artificial species , and it took a year and a half of the bioethical discussions to continue .
每個主要宗教都參與其中	every major religion is involved .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	it's a strange study because a lot of religious leaders are using their creed , their scriptures , and they can't find the doctrines to prohibit life , so there's nothing wrong with that at its most fundamental concern from biological weapons , but only after doing these experiments can we figure out what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	now the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study to identify the risks and benefits of the society and also to develop research for scientific teams like ours , who are building the rules forward , while we're also trying to be a good example .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complicated issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	in addition to bioterrorism , they're all very simple: can we design tools to produce clean energy through various simple steps , or can we shift energy production patterns in the developing world ?
心理學家philipzimbardo說我們大部分人都忽略了幸福和成功的來源:那就是我們觀望過去、面向現在和展望未來 。 要想改善生活質量 , 他建議我們首先要調整時間觀念 。	the psychologist philipzimbardo suggests that most of us overlook the source of happiness and success: that's what we see in the past , in the present and in the present , in the present and in the future , to advise the quality of life , first of all , to adjust our time .
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	you know , happiness , mind , psychology , you're talking about it .
philipzimbardo健康的時間觀念	philip zimbardo has timelapse concepts .
我想跟你們分享一些對時間的神秘力量的看法當然是在很短的時間內	i'd like to share with you some of the mysterious powers of time , of course , in a short period of time .
影片:好的 , 開始計時 。 30秒倒計時	video: ok , start time . 30 seconds counted .
保持安靜 。	stay quiet .
注意時間 。 結束倒計時 。	pay attention to the time . end the time .
10 , 9 , 8 , 76 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......	10 , nine , eight , 76 , five , four , three , two . . .
philipzimbardo:讓我們來看看這段對話是有關 " 亞當的誘惑 "	philip zimbardo: let's take a look at this conversation about " adam's temptation . "
快 , 亞當 , 別磨磨<unk>的 , 就咬一口 , 我已咬過了	soon , adam , don't honey , just bite , i've bitten .
就一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄夏娃	adam . don't give up eve .
我不知道啊	i don't know .
我真的不想惹麻煩	i really don't want to get in trouble .
好吧 , 就一口 。 能怎麼樣 ?	all right , just one bite . what can we do ?
生活中充滿了誘惑 。 而且到處都是:屈服或反抗是、不是、現在、隨後、衝動、沉穩專注現在和展望未來	life is full of temptations , and everywhere: submission or resistance , isn't , now , impulsive , steady focus on the present and the future .

那什麼是時間洞察力呢 ? 這將是我下面要講的	so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about .
時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time perspective is the study of individuals , including us , how to categorize the experiences of time zones or time units .
其實我們一直都在自然而然地做著	we've been doing it naturally .
而影響我們劃分方式的因素有很多 , 包括不同的文化背景、國家個人、社會階層以及不同的教育背景	and there are many factors that influence our drawings , including different cultural backgrounds , the individuals , the social classes , and the different background

對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for those of us who make decisions based on the status quo , we call them " face to present , " because they focus on what's happening now .
對於另一些人來說 , 現正發生什麼並不重要	for others , what's happening doesn't matter .
就好像是說: " 我以前好像經歷過類似的事情 " 一樣	it's like , " i used to be experiencing something similar . "
所以 , 他們基於過去的經驗來做決定	so they've made decisions based on experiences of the past .

我們稱呼這些人為:展望未來 。 因為他們專注於將來會是怎麼樣的	we call these people the future , because they're focused on what's going to happen in the future .

它的大氣有分子態氮組成 , 就像我們現在這個房間一樣不過它的大氣中充滿甲烷、丙烷和乙烷等有機材質	it has molecular nitrogen in its atmosphere , like we do in this room , but its atmosphere is filled with methane , propane and ethane , and organic material .
土衛六上這些分子含量很高這些分子分解後形成煙霧	these molecules are high in titan , and these molecules break down to form smoke .
這些煙霧無處不在 , 瀰漫於整個土衛六	these smoke is everywhere , and it's filled with titan .

類似於地球上的焦油 , 或油什麼的 , 我也不清楚	like the tar on earth or the oil , i don't know .
我們是這樣推測的 。 這些分子尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在土星地溫下是液態的 。	and we speculate that . these molecules , especially methane and ethane , are liquid at ground temperature .
我們發現甲烷就是土星的水 。	and it turns out that methane is the water of saturn .
在大氣裡是可以凝縮的這一發現為許多稀奇古怪的設想提供了可能 。 土星有甲烷雲層 。 甲烷雲層上有數百公里高的霧氣層光線無法穿透雲層射向地面	and in the atmosphere , this discovery of condensation is possible for a number of odd assumptions: methane clouds , methane clouds , hundreds of kilometers in the methane cloud , fog light that doesn't travel through the cloud layers .

雖冷 , 但還有雨	it's cold , but it's rain .

佈德魯斯的抵抗運動的影響從此遍及約旦河西岸的所有村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的巴勒斯坦人居住區	the effect of the resistance movement in derrus has spread over the entire villages in the west bank and in palestinian settlements in jerusalem .
