暴力抵抗和非暴力抵抗有一個非常重要的共同點兩者像一個劇院渴望吸引觀眾的青睞	violence resistance and nonviolent resistance have a very important common denominator , which is what a theater wants to attract audiences .
如果暴力演員總是領銜主演將全球目光聚焦巴勒斯坦問題那麼非暴力領導人就很難向他們的民眾證明和平的反抗才是帶他們脫離苦海的可行方案	if violence actors are always leading titles to focus globally on the palestinian problems , then nonviolent leaders are struggling to prove peaceful resistance to their citizens that it's possible to get them out of the sea .
在座為人父母的估計對關注的力量並不陌生	the estimates of this parenthood are no stranger to the power of attention .
如果孩子第一次鬧脾氣就得到父母的注意那麼你的孩子以後肯定會鬧得更厲害	if your child ever gets a parent's notice for the first time , then your child's going to be even worse .
鬧脾氣就會成為兒童心理學家所說的功能性行為孩子學會用這種方式引起父母的注意	the temple becomes what children's psychologists call functional behavior , and the child learns to catch the attention of their parents in this way .
父母可以透過關注或不予理睬來鼓勵或抑制此行為	parents can encourage or inhibit behavior without ignoring or ignoring it .
而這也適用於成年人	and this applies to adults as well .
事實上社群和國家的行為是能夠受到影響而改變的而這取決於國際社會選擇關注的方面	in fact , social and nation behavior can be affected , and it depends on the aspects of international choice .
我相信解決中東地區的衝突給這裡帶來和平關鍵是我們要透過更多地關注當地的非暴力領袖來把非暴力行動轉變為一種功能性行為	i believe that the key to solving conflict in the middle east is that we need to focus more on local nonviolent leaders to transform nonviolent action into a functional behavior .
在約旦河西岸加沙地帶以及東耶路撒冷地區拍攝那裡的村莊時我親眼目睹了區區一部紀錄片對行為轉變所帶來的影響	in jordan , in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i witnessed firsthand the impact of a documentary film on the transformation of behavior .
在離耶路撒冷很近的一個名叫瓦拉傑的村子那裡的村民面臨著與佈德魯斯相似的困境	in a village , which is very close to jerusalem , called varajeger , the villagers face a plight similar to budrus .
他們即將被包圍起來失去大片土地無法自由進入約旦河西岸或耶路撒冷	they're going to be surrounded and lose big patches of land , losing freedom in the west bank or in jerusalem .
在進行了長達兩年的非暴力抵抗之後他們最終心灰意冷因為他們沒有得到任何人的注意	after two years of conducting nonviolent resistance , they were eventually frustrated because they didn't get attention from anybody .
於是我們在那裡組織播放了紀錄片	so we played the documentary film there .
一週之後他們組織了一場在當時參與人數最多最有紀律的遊行示威	a week later , they organized the most disciplined demonstration to participate at the time .
組織者們說當村民在紀錄片中看到佈德魯斯的故事他們感覺到確實有人與他們志同道合人們是在乎的	the organizers told us that when the villagers saw bandrus in the documentary film , they felt that there was actually someone who cared about it with them .
於是他們沒有放棄	so they didn't give up .
以色列有一個新的和平運動被稱為 " 索裡德拉爾特 " 在希伯來語中意為 " 團結一致 "	israel has a new peace movement called solidarity , " which means " solidarity " in hebrew .
佈德魯斯的故事成為了這個運動的領導者招兵買馬的主要手段之一	the story of dudes became one of the primary means of the campaign recruiting soldiers for horses .
他們反映說那些從未加入任何運動的以色列人看了紀錄片之後瞭解了非暴力抵抗的力量並開始加入他們行動	they reflected that israelis who had never joined in any movement had seen a documentary , understood the power of nonviolent resistance and started joining them in action .
瓦拉傑和索裡德拉爾特運動的例子告訴我們即使是小成本的獨立電影也能夠幫助非暴力抵抗轉變為一種功能性行為	varajeger and solidart's examples suggest that even a smallbusiness film can help nonviolent resistance to a functional behavior .
想象一下主流媒體若是開始報道每週在貝拉因尼亞林瓦拉傑等村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的香克哈拉和西路萬巴勒斯坦居住區裡發生的非暴力示威活動這將產生多麼巨大的力量更多的人會關注非暴力運動領導者重視他們讓他們的工作更有成效	imagine the mainstream media , and if you start reporting about villages like lynvalaj in bella , in jerusalem , and the nonviolent demonstrations that happen in the residential neighborhoods of nonviolence in the west residential neighborhood , it's going to be so powerful that more people will pay attention to nonviolent activists that
我相信最重要的是我們要認識到如果我們不關注這些運動它們就是隱形的彷彿從來沒有發生過	and i think the most important thing we need to recognize is that if we don't focus on these movements , they're invisible as if they've never happened before .
但我以親身經歷為證如果我們關注這些運動就會得到發展	but i'm a proof of personal experience that if we look at these movements , we're going to get to advance .
它們一旦發展其影響力就會遍及巴以衝突	once they're developed , they're influential .
這種影響能夠最終將衝突化解	and this ultimately resolves conflict .
這些領導者證明了非暴力運動在佈德魯斯這樣的地方是可行的	these leaders have proven that nonviolent movements work in places like russia .
我們一起來關注他們讓他們證明這在任何地方都是可行的	and we looked at them , and they showed that this is possible anywhere .
西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simone sneak illustrates the inspiring leadership at the heart of the model , a golden circle , meaning the fundamental source of the leadership quality is the answer " why ? " he listed apple , martin luther king and the successful brotherhood , and recently , losing the typical digital video .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bull seye , entrepreneur , muine , sales , selling success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simone sneak: how great leaders inspire movements .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how do you explain when things are developing unexpectedly ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , what do you mean when someone seems to have successfully and unexpectedly ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why is apple so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	for years , year after year , they were more innovative than all their competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're actually just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they're not the same as the other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	there's the same approach , exposure to the same people , the same agents , the consultants , the media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem to be so remarkable ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	and again , why is it led by martin luther king , the civil rights movement ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at the time in the united states , before the civil rights movement , not only did he suffer from discrimination , but he was also not the only great orator of the age .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	and why is it that the white brothers were able to build a driverspowered airplane , compared to them , the rest of the team at the time seemed to be more capable and more funded ?
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't make a carrier airplane , the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there's got to be something else that's going on .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	i made a discovery about three and a half years ago .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed the way i think about how the world works , and even fundamentally changed the way i work .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's how i discovered a pattern .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i find out that all the great and exciting leaders and organizations in the world , whether it's apple or martin luther king or white brothers , they think , act , communicate in exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but it's the exact opposite of everybody else's .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i'm doing is organizing it . it's probably the simplest concept in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? how ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why some organizations and leaders can inspire and potential where others cannot .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	i'm going to give you a quick explanation of these terms .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	everyone on this planet , every organization , knows what they're doing , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , and you can call them your differences , or your unique crafts , or your unique tradeoffs , or your unique tradeoffs , or whatever it is .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations understand why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	there's nothing to do with " why " and " profit " here .
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profit is just one result , always with one result .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	and by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what's the reason you do that ? what kind of beliefs do you hold ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why does your institution exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why do you get up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why should anyone care about you ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we move , the way we communicate , is all about extroverts .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	obviously , the way we do it is start with clarity and then blur stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but inspiring leaders and organizations , both in size and in their domain , they think , move and communicate , go in the middle .
舉個例子吧 。	let me give you an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i'll give you an apple because it's a simple example , everybody understands it .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple had the same marketing information as any other company , it would have looked like , " we make the best computers .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beauty , using simple , interface friendly .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	do you want to buy one ? " not that much .
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	that's how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way most marketing markets , most of the ways that most sales are adopted , and the way that most of us interact with each other .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our professions are doing , we say how we're different or how we're better than others , and then we expect other people's reactions , like purchasing , voting , etc . , etc .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	this is our new law firm , and we have the best lawyers and the biggest clients , and we can always meet the customer's requests .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new vehicle type , very fuelefficient , dermal seat . buy a car .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" everything we do is about breakthroughs and innovation .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we believe that we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	and the way we challenge the status quo is by designing very beautifully our products , using simple , interface friendly .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we're just making the best computers along the way .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	would you like to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	it feels completely different , right ? you're ready to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	all i did was to reverse the order of the information transmission .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it's been shown to us that people don't buy products that you make , and people buy your beliefs and missions .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products you make , they buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	that's why everyone here takes it for granted when they buy a computer from an apple company .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but when we bought mp3 players from apple , mobile phones or digital cameras , it was also very comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and actually , as i said , apple's just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing that separates the apple from the structural competition .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitors and apple have the same capacity to make all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they've tried it .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , the czech launched a flatscreen tv .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making flatscreen tvs .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	because they've been making flatscreen displays for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the company darre launched an mp3 player and a palmpilot , and they had a very good quality and a very good design , and nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	in fact , at this point , we couldn't imagine buying an mp3 player from darre .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products you make , they buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the goal of the company is not to do business with everybody who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's business with people who have the same ideas that you do .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	that's the most amazing part . none of the ones i'm talking about are my own perspective .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	all of these views can be found from biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the horizontal spectrum of the brain , you'll see that the human brain is actually divided into three main parts , and those three main parts are very well matched with golden
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our latest brain , our jurisdictional brain , or our cerebral cortex , corresponds to this roundabout .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cerebral cortex is responsible for all of our rational and logical thinking and language function .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two parts in the middle are our brains , and the brain is responsible for all of our emotions , such as trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's responsible for all behaviors and decisions , but there's no speech in that part .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we communicate in from extroverts , yes , people understand a lot of complicated information , like characteristics , strength , facts and graphs .
但不足以激發行動 。	but it's not enough to inspire action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're diplomatically communicating from the introverts , we're communicating directly with behavior , and then we're rationally thinking about what we're saying and doing .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	and that's where the inner decisions come from .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show all the data graphs to some people , and they say , " i know what the data and the graph means , but it just doesn't feel right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use that verb , " feeling " ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because the part of the brain that controls decision making doesn't dominate language .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	we just said , " i don't know why , it just doesn't feel right . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or sometimes you're listening to the call , or you're listening to the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but the heart and the soul aren't parts of the control of behavior .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this takes place in your brain , controlling decisionmaking behavior rather than language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you're doing what you're doing , and people are responding to your motivation , then how do you win people's support , buy things from you , or , more importantly , loyal to you and want to be part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	and again , the goal is not just to sell the things that you have to be needed ; it's to sell them to people that share your beliefs .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who share a common belief .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say that if you hire someone just because he can do the job , they're just going to work for your salary , but if you hire someone you share a faith , they'll pay you a hot blood , sweat and tears .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	now , there's no more appropriate example than the white brothers' stories .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most of you have never heard of this man , samuel lanley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion of commitment to motorized robots was like the current website .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everyone was trying .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	samuel lanley has all the components of success .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or your company fail ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are always answering you in the same sequence as three things: lack of funding , bad people , bad posture .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	it's always those three reasons , so let's go through one analysis .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense funded samuel lanley 50 , 000 dollars as a research robot .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so funding is not a problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he's worked at harvard university , and he's learned to work at the smithsonians , and he knows the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he hired domestic talent , and the best people he could attract , and the market conditions were quite profitable .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times did his track records , and everyone supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why haven't you even heard of him ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	meanwhile , hundreds of kilometers away in subton , ohio , orville wright and virgin wright , together with no elements of success .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they didn't have money . they used the income of a bicycle shop to pursue their dreams . none of the wright brothers' teams ever went to college , even oville and virbur . the new york times was more impressed .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	the difference is that what orville and vibel pursued was a career , a goal , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believe that if they can build robots , they'll change the course of development around the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	samuel langley was different .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wanted to finance , he wanted to be famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	he was looking for the end result .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see , let's see what happens .
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	those who have dreams of pregnant with the white brothers are struggling towards the heavens .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	people on the other side are working for salary .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	and the stories that came later said that every time the white brothers went out to experiment , they had to carry the fivepart pieces , because that's how many times they would crash before they came back to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	finally , on december 17th , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody was there .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we didn't know it until a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	later things confirmed the lanley motivation wasn't innocent , and he quit the day that the white brothers were successful .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he was supposed to be able to say , " guys , that's a great invention , and i can improve your technology . "
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to build an airplane , he wouldn't be rich , he wouldn't be famous , so he quit his job .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	people don't buy your products ; they're your beliefs .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	if you talk about your beliefs , you're going to attract people who share your beliefs .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract people who share the same beliefs that you do ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	there's a pattern for innovation , and if you don't know the pattern , you've got this idea .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	2 . 5 percent of our society is innovators .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	13 . 5 percent of people are very , very few adopters in the early days .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34 percent is mostly early accepting and then later accepting the majority and the last .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	the only reason that these guys ended up buying a phone call is because they couldn't buy a dial .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	and while we're different , we're in different positions of this curve , but the pattern of innovation tells us that if you want to be successful in a massmarket , or you want an idea in a popular market , you'll have to wait until you get 15 to 18 percent of the market reception points , and that's when the market really started .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask the company , " what about your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they'll tell you , proudly , " oh , about 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you're likely to be here in 10 percent of the customers .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all get 10 percent of the people to be " meaningful . "
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we typically describe them this way .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling , " oh , they're kind of taking care of god . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how do you find people who will intentionally meet before they haven't become your customers ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	that's the problem , and that's the point where you have to fill this gap , as geoffrey mull said , " cross the divide , " because most of the early things aren't going to try new things unless some people have tried it first .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these guys , the innovators and the early minorities , they like the bold try .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they naturally do things intuitively , from their worldview instincts , not just because of what products on the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this is the first time a group of people came out on the iphone in line for six hours , and in fact , waiting for a week you can go to the store and buy it from the shelves .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a batch of 40 , 000 dollars spent on flatscreen televisions , despite the technologies that weren't there at the time .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and in addition , they're not buying those products because of the advances of technologies , but because of themselves .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they wanted to be the first person to experience a new product .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你的行動只是證明了你的信念 。	people don't buy your products ; people buy your beliefs ; your actions just prove your beliefs .

我們先著眼於大腦海馬區 , 即黃色的區域這是我們的記憶器官 。	let's first look at the hippocampus , the yellow area here is our memory organ .
如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if you have damage to the hippocampus , like those with alzheimer's , you're going to lose memory , and you can't remember where the car is .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	the hippocampus is originated in latin with " hippocampus " because the shape of the hippocampus looks a little bit like " hippocampus . "
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus and other regions of the brain are made of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	the human brain is made up of about 100 billion neurons .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each neuron is communicating a small pulse of electrical impulses through some connections , or some peak peak communication .
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is made up of two layers of cells that are intimately connected .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists understand how spatial memory work and the mechanisms of spatial memory work with spatial memory in a particular environment .
現在想象一下 , 我們正在為這隻老鼠的海馬區中的一個神經元細胞 " 錄影 " 。	now imagine that we're recording a neuron in the hippocampus of this mouse .
每當這個細胞發出小型尖峰電壓 , 隨後會出現一個紅點以及咔噠的一聲 。	every time this cell fires a small peak peak , it'll hit a red dot and a click sound .
我們可以看出每當老鼠進入環境中某一特定位置 , 這個神經元細胞便會有反應 。	we can see that whenever a mouse enters a certain location in the environment , the neuron will respond .
然後這個細胞再透過小型尖峰電壓將以上資訊傳遞給大腦的其它區域 。	and this cell then communicates information to other areas of the brain through a small peak .
這麼一來 , 我們可以憑藉這個細胞傳送訊號的頻率推知老鼠經過的相應位置 。	in this way , we can use this cell to send a signal frequency to predict where the rat goes by .
倘若我們記錄的是很多不同的神經元細胞 , 就會發現當老鼠處於不同的位置上時 , 不同的神經元細胞會產生各自的電訊號 , 正如我們在這些方形中看到的那樣 。	and if we document a lot of different neurons , we find that different neurons will produce their own electrical signals as we see them in these squares .
這些訊號為大腦中的其它區域勾勒出一張地圖 , 持續地向大腦指示出 , " 我現在位於環境中的哪個具體點上 ? "	these signals are mapped in other areas of the brain , constantly instructing to the brain , " what are the specific points of the environment that i'm sitting in ? "
我們也記錄人腦中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 。	we also documented " location neurons in the human brain . "
癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	people with epilepsy sometimes need to monitor their brain electrical activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some patients played a video game where they were driving in a small town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and when they drive over town somewhere in their hippocampus , the positioning neurons in the hippocampus will be inspired , sending signals .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does that position cell know that mice or people are in a position ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	here are two neurons that tell us that the boundaries of the environment are essential .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	the cell above it tends to produce signals as the mouse goes in the middle of the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the box , the activation zone expands .
下面的這個喜歡在老鼠緊鄰南面屏障時作出反應 。	this next preference responds when the rat is clenched on the neighboring south barrier .
因此當你在盒中放入另一屏障時 , 不論老鼠在盒中何處 , 只要它的南面有屏障 , 該細胞中的相應位置便會同時產生訊號 。	so when you put another barrier in the box , wherever the mouse is in the box , if it has a screen in the south , the correspondence in the cell will produce a signal at the same time .
這表明瞭解到達邊界比如周邊的建築物等需要的距離和方向對於海馬區的 " 工作 " 而言至關重要 。	it shows that the distance and direction that arrives at the border around the buildings and the direction around the hippocampus is crucial to the work of the hippocampus .
而且確實 , 在老鼠蒐羅環境時 , 我們在海馬區的輸入訊號中 , 檢測到能對距環境邊界的特定距離與方向作出精確感應的神經元細胞 。	and indeed , in the case of the mouse collecting the environment , we input signals in the hippocampus to detect specific distances and directions of those neurons that are sensitive to the border of the environment .
這裡左邊的細胞 , 你可以看出 , 當老鼠向東靠近邊界或屏障時 , 該細胞都會作出反應 , 不論這邊界是一個方盒的邊還是一個圓柱盒的邊甚至是老鼠繞著轉的桌布的垂簾 。	the cell on the left , as you can see , when the rat approaches the east or closes the barrier , the cell responds , whether it's a boundary or a column box or even a tablecloth around the mice .
而右面的細胞則是在老鼠南面出現邊界時響應 , 不論這邊界是桌布的垂簾還是一堵牆甚至是兩個被隔開的桌子之間的間隙 。	and the cells on the right respond when the border appears on the south side of the mouse , whether it's the tablecloth curtain or the wall between two tables that are separated .
以上是我們所推測的一種 " 定位細胞 " 給動物定位的方式 。	so that's how we speculate that positioning cell to the animals .
我們也可檢測 , 人類在簡單環境中 , 是怎樣給諸如這面旗這樣的物體定位的或者乾脆把這物體想成你的車 。	we can also detect how human beings , in a simple environment , position objects like this or just think of the object as your car .
我們先讓人們熟悉一下環境 , 同時記下物體所在的位置 。	let's get people familiar with the environment and remember where the objects are .
接著 , 再讓他們回到那個環境 , 通常他們都能根據記憶準確無誤地標出物體所在的位置 。	and then return them to that environment , usually they're able to tag objects based on memory accurately where they are .
但在一些試驗中 , 我們會改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 正如我們在 " 定位細胞 " 實驗中所做的那樣 。	but in some trials , we're going to change the shape and the scale of the environment , just like we did in the positioning cell experiment .
如此 , 我們可以透過研究實驗者改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 來了解旗幟發生了怎樣的位移	in this way , we can change the shape and the scale of the flag by studying the experimenter .
比如現在你所看到的 , 假設這面旗幟在如圖中小四方形內的 " × " 的位置 , 然後接著你問人們小旗在哪 , 但實際上你已經將總環境的尺度擴大了 , 結果他們所認為的旗所在的位置也相應地向外擴張 , 而這擴張的模式和 " 定位細胞 " 的一模一樣 。	so what you're seeing here , for example , is if the flag is in the quadrillion location of the xx , and then you ask people where the flag is , but you've actually expanded the size of the total environment , and it turns out that the flag is identical to the expansion of that pattern , and that expanding pattern is exactly what the position cell looks like .
這就好像你是透過儲存被某一特定位置所激發的 " 定位細胞 " 產生的訊號模式來記憶小旗的位置的 , 接著當你回到那個地點的時候 , 透過四處打量 , 便可以將你當前腦中 " 定位細胞 " 的訊號模式與之前的模式進行匹配 。	it's as if you're storing the signal patterns that are generated by a particular location that are firing to remember the flag , and then when you go back to that location , you can match the signal patterns of your previously positioned cell through everywhere .
這個過程便可讓你回到 " 老地方 " 。	and the process takes you back to old places .
我們也能透過位移來給自己定位 。	we can also target ourselves through our positions .
因此當我們外出時或許是我們停車後下來隨便走走我們可以給自己定位 , 因為我們可以粗略地將自己的運動路線與大體的返回方向進行整合 。	so when we're outside , maybe we stop and we're offering ourselves a position , because we can integrate our motor trajectory with our bodies roughly .
" 定位細胞 " 也能從一種叫做 " 網狀細胞 " 的細胞那兒獲得此類線路整合的資訊 。	positioning cells can also receive information from a cell called net cells , like this integrated circuit .
目前在向海馬區的訊號輸入中又發現了 " 網狀細胞 " , 它們與 " 定位細胞 " 有點類似 。	and what we're finding now in the hippocampus is that they're a little bit similar to what we call positioning cells .
隨著老鼠的 " 四處探索 " , 每一個神經元細胞被大量各種位置所激發的訊號組合在一起 , 貫穿整個環境構成一個令人驚歎的規整的三角網格 。	as mice explore around , each neuron is assembled by massive locations of signals stirring throughout the environment to make a spectacular triangular grid .
倘若你對一系列 " 網狀細胞 " 進行記錄這裡以不同的顏色區分每一個細胞發出的訊號都能形成網狀 , 遍及整個環境 , 而且每一個細胞的網狀訊號集的位置都與其他細胞有一定偏差 。	if you document a series of " mesh cells " signals that distribute in different colors , each cell can form a mesh , all over the environment , and each cell’s mesh collection has a slightly worse position than the other cells .
因此紅色標註的細胞訊號集合在這個網格上 , 綠色的是這個 , 而藍色的是這個 。	so the cellular signals that are tagged in red are gathered together on this grid , and that's the green one , and that's the blue one .
因此綜合來看 , 這就好像老鼠可以在它所到達的環境中建立一個虛擬的位置訊號網這就有點像你在地圖上所看到的經線和緯線 , 只不過要將線替換成 " 三角形 " 。	so in a synthesis , it's as if the rat could build a virtual location network in its arrival environment , kind of like the lines and latitudes you see on the map , except for replacing the lines with triangles .
當老鼠移動的時候 , 這些電訊號能透過這些細胞傳遞給下一個神經元細胞從而為老鼠定位 , 這樣老鼠就能在運動時知道自己身在何處 。	and as the mouse moves , these electrical signals can be transmitted to the next neuron from these cells so that the mouse can know where they're moving .
那麼人類是否有 " 網狀細胞 " 呢 ?	so , do we have net cells ?
因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because all the signals collectively have the same symmetry and the same grid fluctuations here in orange red , suggesting that the changes in all the networking cells in the brain should depend on whether we're moving in six directions or whether we're moving in six directions between six directions .
我們可以為人們做核磁共振掃描 , 與此同時讓他們玩一個小型電子遊戲 , 還是之前所說的那個遊戲 , 然後來看看當時的訊號 。	we can do mri scans for people , and we can get them to play a little video game , or that game , and see what the signals were .
啊哈沒錯 , 你在人腦中的內嗅皮層上看到了網狀細胞 , 而它們出現的位置和老鼠的網狀細胞在大腦中所出現的位置一樣 。	aha , yeah , you see the net cells in the human brain , and they're located exactly the same location as the mice's mesh cells are in the brain .
現在我們回頭看看荷馬 。	now let's go back to homer .
他可能憑藉與周邊建築以及四周邊界的相對距離和方向來回憶他的車停在哪兒 。	he could recall where his car was parked by relative distances and directions from the surrounding border .
而那將由專門 " 檢測邊界 " 的神經元細胞發出的訊號來執行 。	and that's going to be run by a signal that's going to be published by the neurons from the border specialized .
他可能也記得自己是怎麼從停車場走出來的 , 而這就有賴於網狀細胞發出訊號了 。	and he probably remembers how he came out of the parking lot , and it relied on the signaling of a network cell .
這兩種型別的神經元細胞都可以啟用 " 定位細胞 " 。	these two different types of neurons can be activated with " positioning cells . "
因此荷馬成功折返的方法便是在走動中尋求與他之前停車時腦中所建立的訊號集樣式最為匹配的一個腦中即時形成的訊號集樣式 。	so homer's successful folding returns to the successful clustering of signals that came out of his previous parking brain in the most immediately matched samples in a brain .
而那就能將他領回 " 老地方 " 了 , 這個過程與最終的目標視物無關不論他的車是否還在那兒他都能找到停車點 。	and that allows him to return to the old place , which isn't about the ultimate goal , whether or not his car is still there , he's going to find a parking spot .
或許車已經被拖走了 ,	maybe the car has been dragged out .
但他仍然知道車原來停在哪 , 因此他會回到原位去取車 。	but he still knew where the car was stopping , so he would go back to the original vehicle .
撇開 " 空間記憶力 " 而言 , 倘若我們單獨觀察這種網狀訊號集在整個大腦中的活動情況 , 就會發現這種訊號形式分佈廣泛 , 每當我們需要回憶一些自己過去的經歷時這種網狀的訊號形式就會活躍起來 , 譬如 , 當你試圖回憶上次參加婚禮的情況時	and aside from this " spatial memory , " if we alone observed the activity of this mesh in the entire brain , this signal was spread across a wide range of sizes , and every time we needed to recall some of the experiences of our past , this mesh form would activate , like when you were trying to recall the previous wedding .
因此有可能 , 神經元細胞再現空間的功能也參與視覺畫面的呈現這樣當我們試圖回憶一個曾經置身其中的場面時 , 至少可以藉助想象而勾勒出整個場景 。	so it's possible that neurons reconstruct the function of the space and also the representation of the visuals that we're trying to recall a scene where we've been , at least , in imagination .
倘若事實果真如此 , 記憶的形成就開始於: " 定位細胞 " 透過這些縝密的連結相互啟用然後 " 邊界感應細胞 " 被再次啟用從而形成我們視點周圍的場景的空間格局 。	and if that's true , the formation of memory begins to be adapted through these very careful connections , and the border sensory cells are reactivated again to form the spatial space of the surrounding scenes .
網狀細胞可以使視點穿透那個空間 。	the net cells can get your perspective through that space .
而另一種 " 方位細胞 " , 我之前沒有提到它 , 它們像指南針一樣 , 都是根據你的朝向來作出反應的 。	and the other digital cell , which i didn't mention earlier , they respond to as compasses that respond to you based on where you're headed .
它們可以明確你需要在腦中形成哪個方位的影象 , 就拿回憶婚禮情景來說 , 以上過程就能讓你回想起那一切 。	they're going to be able to specify which part of the brain you're going to need to form in the brain , take back the wedding scenario , and remind you of all of that .
好了 , 以上就是在認知神經科學領域所開闢的新紀元 , 在這個領域中 , 我們開始嘗試從大腦中數以億計的單個神經元細胞的行為出發 , 來了解人類心理活動產生的過程 。 比如人們是如何記憶、想象甚至思考的	all right , so that's the new era in the field of cognitive neuroscience , where we're trying to publish the behavior of hundreds of millions of individual neurons in the brain to understand how human psychological activity is produced by memory , imagination , and even even thinking .
謝謝各位 。	thank you .
想象一個由合作多部門 , 多政府 , 公私力量組成的全球安全 。 這不僅是開放安全支持者的幻想 , 而是jamesstavridis , 北約最高長官的設想 , 他從分享了從現代軍事史的生動瞬間到解釋了為什麼要靠修橋而不是修牆來構築未來安全 。	imagine a collaborative , multiple governments , multiple private forces , which isn't just an illusion of opensource supporters but of james staviss , the tallest officer in north , who shared the instant moments of the military history to explain why to build a security future on bridges rather than fixing a wall .
collaboration , globalissues , open-source , peace , politics , socialmedia , violence , war	collaboration , global isisues , open source , peaceti , litics , lawmedia , violence , warrior .
jamesstavridis:北約的最高長官如何看待全球安全	james stavridis: the top officials of northern dating look at global security .
我將要介紹一些開放式安全性問題 , 因為我們在21世紀已經離安全越來越近了 。	i'm going to talk about some opensource security issues , because we're getting closer and closer to security in the 21st century .
我們先回顧一下20世紀吧 , 然後我們就能瞭解安全這個概念是如何為我們而工作 。	let's go back to the 20th century , and then we can understand how this idea of security works for us .
這裡是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。	this is verdun , a battlefield in france , just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .
1916年 , 在verdun這個戰場上 , 700000人在300天內被殺了 , 那就是差不多2000人一天 。	in 1916 , in verdun , 7 , 000 people were killed in 300 days , almost 2 , 000 people .
咱們繼續往前看--20世紀的安全--看到二戰 , 我們看得到在斯大林格勒保衛戰 , 300天內有二百萬人戰死 。	let's keep looking forward 20thcentury security seeing world war ii , we can see the stalingrade war , and 300 days , two million people died .
進入冷戰 , 我們繼續建造圍牆 。	we went into the cold war and we continued to build the walls .
我們從一戰的壕溝 , 到二戰的馬其頓防線 , 再到冷戰中的鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。	we went from the trench warfare of the first world war to the macedonian line of the second world war , to the iron curtains of the cold war , the berlin wall .
所以我今天的主題是為了完成 " 安全 " 這個目標 , 我們不建造牆 , 而建造橋 。	so my thesis today is to accomplish safety , we don't build walls and build bridges .
在歐洲有一個很著名的橋 。	there's a very famous bridge in europe .
它在drina河上 , 是作家ivoandric的一個小說的主題 , 這部小說講述了如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區最動盪的部分大量的牆被築起 。	it's on the drina river , and it's the subject of a novel by the writer hivo andric , and it describes the most turbulent part of how to build in europe and the balkans .
而最近 , 也就是在近十年 , 我們開始看到這些地區開始 , 儘管有些猶豫不決 , 逐漸融合在一起 。	and recently , in the last decade , we've begun to see these regions start to hesitate despite a little bit of integration .
我想再次重申 , 開放式安全是關於聯絡國際的不同地區的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的和公共的 , 並且把它們透過戰略性溝通 , 在社交網上聯絡在一起 。	i want to repeat that , again , opensource security is about contact international , interagency , privatepublic , and connecting them through strategic communication on social networks .
所以 , 接下來我將說一些為什麼我們需要那麼做 , 因為我們的共同目標正在受到威脅 , 而且是多方面的 , 同時沒有一種威脅能被透過築牆隔離解決 。	so i'm going to talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our common goals are being threatened , and in many ways , and there's not a threat being resolved by building walls .

兩萬億每年 。	two trillion dollars a year .

當他被治好他的重度近視是 , 他突然抬頭 , 然後說: " mama , veoelmundo. "	when he was healed his weight , he looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "

這張照片是棒球運動員 。	this is a photograph of a baseball player .

他們是每側最邊上的兩位 。 這是棒球診所的一部分 , 在這裡我們嘗試棒球聯賽 , 國務院 , 在軍隊中的棒球運動員 , 也就是那些能真正上戰場的人 , 之間的合作 , 並且他們把這種診所開到了拉丁美洲和加勒比地區 , 開到了宏都拉斯 , 開到了尼加拉瓜 , 開到了所有中美洲和加勒比的棒球很流行國家 , 而且它創造了安全感 。	they're the two people on each side . this is part of a baseball clinic , where we've tried baseball leagues , state departments , baseball players in the military , collaborations between people who can actually go to war , and they've created this clinic in latin america and caribbean areas , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all the central american and caribbean baseball nations , which is fashionable , and it creates security .

維基百科是靠每天數萬人的更新 , 數百萬人的提取資訊而建立的 。	wikipedia is built every day by updating tens of thousands of people extracting information from each other .
